Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Standard Method of Salat al-Khawf
Definition and method of the fear prayer with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the standard method of Salat al-Khawf when the congregation fights and prays behind one imam, and identify the key steps.

Core Idea
Salat al-Khawf divides the congregation into two groups to allow simultaneous guarding and prayer.

This passage from Nur al-Idah details the permissibility and method of the Fear Prayer. When the congregation is engaged in battle and agrees to pray behind one imam, a special procedure is followed to ensure security while fulfilling the obligatory prayer. The imam leads each group in turn, and the prayer is completed in a coordinated manner.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for permissibility
Find in the text what makes Salat al-Khawf permissible. Note that it requires the presence of an enemy or fear of drowning or burning.
This is the external cause (sabab) that triggers the concession.
2
Describe the division of the congregation
When the people are fighting and pray behind one imam, he divides them into two groups: one faces the enemy, the other prays with him. Understand the roles.
The imam leads only one group at a time.
3
Outline the prayer sequence for each group
For a two-rak'ah prayer (e.g., Fajr), the imam prays one rak'ah with the first group, then they go to face the enemy. The second group then prays the remaining rak'ah with the imam. For four-rak'ah or Maghrib, he prays two rak'ahs with each group.
The timings of transition differ based on prayer type.
4
Explain the recitation rules
The first group, after returning, completes its remaining rak'ahs without recitation (since they already heard the imam's recitation). The second group may recite if they wish.
Recitation is a sunnah, not obligatory, in these later rak'ahs.
5
Note the requirement to walk and direction
The group that has prayed must go to the enemy walking, and only in the direction facing the enemy. If they ride or walk in a different direction, the prayer is invalid.
Walking is the required mode; riding is reserved for extreme fear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة صلاة الخوف باب صلاة الخوف هي جائزة بحضور عدو، وبخوف غرق أو حرق، وإذا تنازع القوم في الصلاة خلف إمام واحدٍ فيجعلهم طائفتين واحدة بإزاء العَدُوِّ ، ويصلي بالأخرى ركعة من الثنائِيَّةِ [الإمام أي الطائفة الأخرى] وركعتين من الرُّباعِيَّةِ أو المغرب، وتمضي هذه إلى العدو مشاة، وجاءت تلك، [بهم الطائفة جمع ماش] ما بقي، وسلم وحده، فذهبوا إلى العَدُوّ، ثم جاءت الأولى وأتموا بلا قراءة [من الصلاة مشاة الطائفة الأولى] فصلی وسلموا ومضوا، ثم جاءت الأخرى إن شاؤوا صلوا ما بقي بقراءة، وإن اشتَدَّ [إلى العدو الطائفة الأخرى. في مكانهم من الصلاة] الخوف صلوا ركبانا فرادى بالإيماء إلى أي جهة قدروا ولم تجز بلا حضور عدو، [صلاة الخوف هي جائزة أي صلاة الخوف بالصفة الآتية. فيجعلهم طائفتين: عم كلامه المقيم خلف المسافر، حتى يقضي ثلاثا بلا قراءة إن كان الأولى، وبقراءة إن كان من من الثانية، والمسبوق إن أدرك ركعة من الشفع، فهو من أهل الأولى، وإلا فمن الثانية واعلم أن الطائفة التي صلت مع الإمام إنما تمضي للعدو في الثنائي بعد ما رفع رأسه من السجدة الثانية، وفي غير الثنائي إذا قام الإمام من التشهد الأول إلى الثانية [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٥٥] الثنائية كالصبح والمقصورة بالسفر والجمعة والعيد وركعتين: أي وصلى بالأولى المذكورة ركعتين. مراقي الفلاح: ٥٥٥] مشاة فإن ركبوا أو مشوا لغير جهة الاصطفاف بمقابلة العدو بطلت. [مراقي الفلاح ٥٥٦ وجاءت تلك الطائفة التي كانت في الحراسة، فأحرموا مع الإمام. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٥٦] معنى وإن اشتد الخوف: أن لا يدعهم العدو بأن يصلوا نازلين بل يهجمونهم بالمحاربة، اشتداد الخوف هنا هو فيصلون ركباناً فرادى؛ وذلك لأن الصلاة على الدابة تجوز بعذر دون هذا العذر، فلأن يجوز بهذا أولى. (الكفاية) ركبانا: قيد بالركوب؛ لأنه لا يجوز ماشياً في غير المصر؛ لأن المشي عمل كثير مفسد للصلاة كالغريق السابح. البحر الرائق: ٢٦٧/٢] فرادی جمع فرد على غير قياس وهو حال كما أن ركبانا كذلك من الأحوال المترادفة أو المتداخلة، قيد بقوله: "فرادى"؛ لأنه لا يجوز بجماعة؛ لعدم الاتحاد في المكان إلا إذا كان راكباً مع الإمام على دابة واحدة فإنه يجوز اقتداء المتأخر منهما بالمتقدم اتفاقاً. [البحر الرائق: ٢٦٧/٢] ولم تجز: أي لا تجوز صلاة الخوف من غير حضور عدو ؛ لعدم الضرورة، حتى لو رأوا سوادا فظنوا أنه عدو، فصلوا صلاة الخوف ثم بان أنه ليس بعدو أعادوها؛ لما قلنا إلا إذا بان لهم قبل أن يتجاوزوا الصفوف، فإن لهم أن يبنوا استحساناً، وهذا كله في حق القوم، وأما الإمام فصلاته جائزة بكل حال؛ لعدم المفسد في حقه. [البحر الرائق: ٢٦٧/٢] ويستحب حمل السلاح في الصلاة عند الخوف وإن لم يتنازعوا في الصلاة خلف إمام واحد، فالأفضل صلاة كل طائفة بإمام مثل حالة الأمن. [القوم] وإن لم يتنازعوا فتذهب الأولى بعد تمامها، ثم تجيء الأخرى، فتصلي بإمام آخر. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٥٧]
The Book of Prayer. Prayer of Fear. Chapter of Prayer of Fear: It is permissible in the presence of an enemy, and with fear of drowning or burning. And if the people are contending [i.e., fighting] and pray behind one imam, he makes them two groups: one facing the enemy, and he prays with the other one rak'ah of a two-rak'ah prayer, and two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer or Maghrib, and this one goes to the enemy walking, and that one comes, [those people, the group, plural of 'walker'] the remainder, and he gives salam alone, so they go to the enemy, then the first comes and they complete without recitation [of the prayer, walking, the first group]. They pray and give salam and go, then the other comes; if they wish, they pray what remains with recitation. And if the fear intensifies [to the enemy, the other group, in their place of prayer] they pray riding, individually, with gesture, towards any direction they can. And it is not permissible without the presence of an enemy. [Prayer of fear: it is permissible, i.e., the prayer of fear in the following description: he makes them two groups: his statement includes the resident behind the traveler, so that he completes three without recitation if he is from the first, and with recitation if he is from the second; and the person who is preceded [latecomer] if he has caught one rak'ah of the even-numbered prayer, then he is from the people of the first, otherwise from the second. And know that the group that prayed with the imam only goes to the enemy in a two-rak'ah prayer after he raises his head from the second prostration, and in other than two-rak'ah when the imam stands from the first tashahhud to the second. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 555] Two-rak'ah prayers like Fajr, shortened prayer on travel, Friday, and Eid, and two rak'ahs: i.e., he prays with the aforementioned first group two rak'ahs. [Maraqi al-Falah: 555] Walking: if they ride or walk to other than the direction of facing the enemy, the prayer is invalid. [Maraqi al-Falah: 556] And that group which was in guarding comes and enters into prayer with the imam. [Maraqi al-Falah: 556] Meaning: And if fear intensifies: that the enemy does not let them pray while descending, but they attack them with fighting; the intensification of fear here is that they pray riding, individually; because prayer on an animal is permitted for an excuse without this excuse, so for it to be permitted with this is more appropriate. (Al-Kifaya) Riding: a restriction to riding; because it is not permissible walking outside the settlement; because walking is a lot of action that invalidates prayer, like the drowning swimmer. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/267] 'Individually' is a plural of 'fard' against analogy, and it is a circumstantial adverb just as 'riding' is also from the overlapping or successive circumstantial adverbs; it is restricted by his saying 'individually' because it is not permissible in congregation due to lack of unity of place, except if he is riding with the imam on one animal, then following of the latter by the former is permissible by agreement. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/267] And it is not permissible: i.e., the prayer of fear is not permissible without the presence of an enemy due to lack of necessity; so if they see a darkness and think it is an enemy, and pray the fear prayer, then it becomes clear that it is not an enemy, they repeat it for what we said, except if it became clear to them before they pass the rows, then they may build upon it by istihsan. And all this is regarding the people; as for the imam, his prayer is valid in all cases because there is no invalidating factor on his part. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/267] And it is recommended to carry weapons in prayer during fear. And if they are not contending [fighting] and pray behind one imam, then the better is for each group to pray with an imam like the state of security. [The people] And if they are not contending, the first group goes after completing it, then the other comes and prays with another imam. [Maraqi al-Falah: 557]
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah is a ruling statement on Salat al-Khawf (Prayer of Fear). It is presented as a matn with interlinear glosses and marginal references from later works like Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, Maraqi al-Falah, Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, and Al-Kifaya. The author begins by defining Salat al-Khawf as permissible (jāʾiz) when an enemy is present or there is fear of drowning or burning. This establishes the condition for its validity: the existence of a genuine threat. The passage then describes the method when the congregation is fighting and agrees to pray behind one imam. The imam divides them into two groups: one faces the enemy, and the other prays with him. For a two-rak'ah prayer (e.g., Fajr), he prays one rak'ah with the group; for four-rak'ah prayers or Maghrib, he prays two rak'ahs with them. The group that prayed then goes to face the enemy, and the second group comes and completes the prayer with the imam. After the imam gives salam, the first group returns and completes their prayer without recitation (since they already heard the imam's recitation), while the second group may recite if they wish. In extreme fear (e.g., active combat), they can pray riding individually, making gestures instead of bowing and prostrating, facing any direction possible. The text emphasizes that the prayer is not valid without the presence of an enemy (or equivalent fear), and if they mistakenly think a crowd is an enemy, they must repeat the prayer unless they realize the error before leaving the rows, in which case they can continue by istihsan. The imam's prayer is always valid because he is not distracted. Finally, the passage recommends carrying weapons during the fear prayer, and when there is no actual fighting, it is better for each group to pray separately with their own imam as in normal conditions.

Key Terms
صلاة الخوف (salat al-khawf): A special form of congregational prayer performed during conditions of fear (e.g., enemy attack, natural disaster) allowing deviations from normal prayer procedures.
طائفتين (ta'ifatayn): Two groups into which the congregation is divided during Salat al-Khawf: one prays with the imam while the other guards against the enemy.
مشاة (mushāh): Walking, i.e., the group that has prayed goes to face the enemy on foot, not riding.
ركبانا (rukbānan): Riding on animals, allowed in extreme fear when they cannot pray on the ground.
فرادى (furādā): Individually, i.e., each person prays alone, not in congregation, when fear is intense.
إيماء (īmā'): Gesture, a substitute for bowing and prostration when unable to perform physical movements due to intense fear.
استحسان (istihsān): Juristic preference; in this context, if the mistake (thinking a crowd is an enemy) is realized before leaving the rows, they may continue the prayer without restarting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the permissibility condition for Salat al-Khawf according to the passage?
A) It is permissible only when the enemy is present and actively attacking.
B) It is permissible with the presence of an enemy or fear of drowning or burning.
C) It is permissible only in extreme fear when riding is necessary.
D) It is permissible without any condition as long as the congregation agrees.

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Khawf is a permissible method of performing the obligatory prayer when facing an enemy or similar danger, using a two-group system to ensure security.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
7 min
Extreme Cases and Conditions of Salat al-Khawf
Extreme forms and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rules for extreme fear (riding, gestures, individual prayer) and for mistakes regarding the enemy's presence, including the use of istihsan.

Core Idea
In extreme fear, prayer reduces to individual gestures on horseback; a mistaken fear requires repetition unless realised before leaving the rows.

This lesson continues with Salat al-Khawf by examining the extreme case where fear is intensified—enemy attacks prevent even standing prayer. The passage also addresses what happens when people mistakenly believe an enemy is present and how the school uses juristic preference (istihsan) to avoid repeating the prayer when the mistake is caught early.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for extreme fear
Find in the text what qualifies as extreme fear (اشتد الخوف). Note that it occurs when the enemy attacks such that people cannot pray on the ground.
This is a greater degree of fear than the standard case.
2
Describe the extreme form of prayer
In extreme fear, they pray riding individually, making gestures (īmā') for bowing and prostration, facing any direction they can.
Gestures are made with the head; prostration gesture is lower than bowing.
3
Explain why walking is not allowed in extreme fear
Walking is considered excessive action that invalidates prayer, similar to a drowning person swimming. Hence, riding is the only option.
Riding is an excuse due to necessity.
4
Analyze the mistake scenario
If people see a dark mass and think it's an enemy, pray Salat al-Khawf, then realize it was not an enemy, they must repeat the prayer. However, if they realize before leaving the rows, they may continue by istihsan.
Istihsan overrides strict qiyas in this case.
5
Note the imam's exception
The imam's prayer is always valid in all cases because there is no invalidating factor on his part.
The imam is considered less distracted.

Source Text

The Book of Prayer. Prayer of Fear. Chapter of Prayer of Fear: It is permissible in the presence of an enemy, and with fear of drowning or burning. And if the people are contending [i.e., fighting] and pray behind one imam, he makes them two groups: one facing the enemy, and he prays with the other one rak'ah of a two-rak'ah prayer, and two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer or Maghrib, and this one goes to the enemy walking, and that one comes, [those people, the group, plural of 'walker'] the remainder, and he gives salam alone, so they go to the enemy, then the first comes and they complete without recitation [of the prayer, walking, the first group]. And if the fear intensifies [to the enemy, the other group, in their place of prayer] they pray riding, individually, with gesture, towards any direction they can. For a two-rak'ah prayer (e.g., Fajr), he prays one rak'ah with the group; for four-rak'ah prayers or Maghrib, he prays two rak'ahs with them. The group that prayed then goes to face the enemy, and the second group comes and completes the prayer with the imam. After the imam gives salam, the first group returns and completes their prayer without recitation (since they already heard the imam's recitation), while the second group may recite if they wish. In extreme fear (e.g., active combat), they can pray riding individually, making gestures instead of bowing and prostrating, facing any direction possible. The text emphasizes that the prayer is not valid without the presence of an enemy (or equivalent fear), and if they mistakenly think a crowd is an enemy, they must repeat the prayer unless they realize the error before leaving the rows, in which case they can continue by istihsan. The imam's prayer is always valid because he is not distracted. Finally, the passage recommends carrying weapons during the fear prayer, and when there is no actual fighting, it is better for each group to pray separately with their own imam as in normal conditions.

Key Terms
صلاة الخوف (salat al-khawf): A special form of congregational prayer performed during conditions of fear (e.g., enemy attack, natural disaster) allowing deviations from normal prayer procedures.
طائفتين (ta'ifatayn): Two groups into which the congregation is divided during Salat al-Khawf: one prays with the imam while the other guards against the enemy.
مشاة (mushāh): Walking, i.e., the group that has prayed goes to face the enemy on foot, not riding.
ركبانا (rukbānan): Riding on animals, allowed in extreme fear when they cannot pray on the ground.
فرادى (furādā): Individually, i.e., each person prays alone, not in congregation, when fear is intense.
إيماء (īmā'): Gesture, a substitute for bowing and prostration when unable to perform physical movements due to intense fear.
استحسان (istihsān): Juristic preference; in this context, if the mistake (thinking a crowd is an enemy) is realized before leaving the rows, they may continue the prayer without restarting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a group prays Salat al-Khawf due to mistaken enemy, but realizes before leaving the rows?
A) They must repeat the prayer.
B) They continue the prayer by istihsan.
C) They stop the prayer and restart later.
D) The prayer is invalid and they must make it up.

Key Takeaway
Extreme fear permits riding, gestures, and individual prayer; mistaken enemy requires repetition unless caught early.

Fear Prayer: Weapons and Group Arrangement
Ruling on carrying weapons and optimal prayer arrangement in fear.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended arrangements for Salat al-Khawf according to the Hanafi school and identify when it is better to pray in separate groups.

Core Idea
In fear prayer, carry weapons; if not fighting, pray separately with your own imam.

This lesson explains the Hanafi rulings for the Fear Prayer (Salat al-Khawf). When there is fear of the enemy, it is recommended to carry weapons during prayer. If the Muslims are not actively fighting, there are two valid arrangements: either all pray together behind one imam, or each group prays separately with its own imam, with the first group finishing before the second begins.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being discussed? It is Salat al-Khawf (fear prayer). What is the ruling on carrying weapons? It is mustahabb (recommended).
The text uses 'yuistahabbu' indicating recommendation, not obligation.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
The text mentions two situations: when the Muslims are fighting ('tanazu'u') and when they are not fighting. The ruling differs based on this.
Fighting means actual combat; otherwise, it is considered a state of safety relative to prayer.
3
Understand the preferred method when not fighting
When not fighting, it is better (afdal) for each group to pray separately behind its own imam, similar to normal prayer. This is to maintain security and focus.
The phrase 'mithl halat al-amn' indicates the prayer should be performed as in safety.
4
Note the sequence for separate groups
If they choose not to fight, the first group completes their prayer entirely, then the second group comes and prays with another imam. This ensures both groups perform a complete prayer without interruption.
The text specifies 'tadhhab al-ula ba'da tamamiha' (the first goes after its completion).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستحب حمل السلاح في الصلاة عند الخوف وإن لم يتنازعوا في الصلاة خلف إمام واحد، فالأفضل صلاة كل طائفة بإمام مثل حالة الأمن. وإن لم يتنازعوا فتذهب الأولى بعد تمامها، ثم تجيء الأخرى، فتصلي بإمام آخر.
And it is recommended to carry weapons in prayer during fear. If they do not fight, then praying behind one imam, then the better is for each group to pray with an imam like the state of safety. And if they do not fight, then the first group goes after completing it, then the other comes and prays with another imam.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage states the rulings for Salat al-Khawf (Fear Prayer) according to the Hanafi school. It is recommended to carry weapons during the prayer when there is fear of the enemy. If the Muslims are not actively engaged in fighting, there are two possibilities: (1) They can all pray together behind one imam, but it is better for each group to pray separately with its own imam, just as in a state of safety. (2) If they choose not to fight while praying, the best method is for the first group to complete their prayer first, then the second group comes and prays with a different imam. This ensures security while fulfilling the obligation of prayer.

Key Terms
صلاة الخوف (Salat al-Khawf): The specific form of congregational prayer performed during battle or when there is fear of the enemy.
مثل حالة الأمن (mithl halat al-amn): Like the state of safety, meaning the normal prayer without fear.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In fear prayer, carry weapons (mustahabb), and if not fighting, pray separately in groups sequentially with separate imams.

Rulings for the Dying Person: Tawjeeh and Talqin
Sunnah actions for the dying person.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunnah actions for the dying person and explain the correct method of talqin.

Core Idea
Tawjeeh and talqin are sunnah, not obligation, done gently without insistence.

This lesson begins the funeral rulings with the compassionate care prescribed for one approaching death. The Shariah does not burden the dying but facilitates a peaceful transition through gentle guidance. These actions are sunnah and mustahab, reflecting respect for the sanctity of the final moments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three actions
From the passage, extract the actions: tawjeeh (turning to qibla), talqin (prompting shahada), and visitation (ziyarah).
These are not obligations but recommended acts.
2
Determine the ruling degree
Note that tawjeeh and talqin are explicitly sunnah (يسن), while visitation is mustahab (يستحب).
Sunnah here means recommended, not obligatory.
3
Note the method for tawjeeh
The dying person should be turned on his right side, or if that is difficult, lying on his back with head raised so his face faces the qibla.
Comfort is considered; the goal is orientation towards qibla.
4
Note the method for talqin
Prompting is done near death without insistence (من غير إلحاح). The dying person is not commanded to say it.
The phrase لا يؤمر بها emphasizes that it is a gentle reminder, not a command.
5
Recognize the difference on talqin after burial
There is a view that talqin in the grave is prescribed (مشروع) and a view that it is not (قيل: لا يلقن). The text leaves it as a difference.
This shows scholarly ikhtilaf on post-burial practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يسن توجيه المحتضر للقبلة على يمينه وجاز الاستلقاء ويرفع رأسه قليلا، ويلقن بذكر من قرب من الموت على ظهره ليصير وجهه إلى القبلة الشهادتين عنده من غير إلحاح، ولا يؤمر بها، وتلقينه في القبر مشروع، وقيل: لا يلقن، فلا يقال له قل بعد ما وضع في القبر وقيل: لا يؤمر به ولا ينهى عنه ويستحب لأقرباء المحتضر وجيرانه الدخول عليه،
It is sunnah to direct the dying person towards the qibla on his right side, and lying on his back is permissible, and his head is raised slightly. He is prompted with the mention of the two testimonies near the time of death without insistence, and he is not commanded to say them. Prompting him in the grave is prescribed, and it is said: he is not prompted, so he is not told 'say' after he is placed in the grave. And it is said: he is not commanded nor forbidden. And it is recommended for the relatives of the dying and his neighbors to visit him.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage states the opening rulings of the funeral chapter. The dying person (muhtadhar) should be turned towards the qibla on his right side; it is also permissible for him to lie on his back with head raised so his face faces the qibla. It is sunnah to prompt him with the shahada (la ilaha illallah) gently without insistence, as the time is difficult. After burial, there is a difference: some say prompting is prescribed, others say not to say 'say' to him. Visiting by relatives and neighbors is recommended.

Key Terms
المحتضر (al-muhtadhar): The person who is dying, in the throes of death.
التلقين (al-talqin): Prompting the dying person to recite the shahada.
الشهادتين (al-shahadatayn): The two testimonies: 'La ilaha illallah, Muhammadur Rasulullah'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is obligatory
B) It is sunnah
C) It is haram
D) It is makruh

Key Takeaway
Tawjeeh and talqin are sunnah actions performed gently for the dying, reflecting mercy and remembrance of Allah.

Recitation and Presence of Impure Individuals at the Deathbed
Rulings on reciting Quran at the dying and excluding menstruating/postpartum women

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended surahs for recitation at the deathbed and explain the Hanafi position on the presence of menstruating, postpartum, and junub persons.

Core Idea
Surah Ya-Sin is recited; women in menstruation/postpartum and junub persons should ideally be removed, but it is not obligatory.

This passage from Nur al-Idah addresses two practices at the deathbed: reciting Qur'an, particularly Surah Ya-Sin, and the issue of who should be present. The Hanafi school considers these rulings important for honoring the dying moment and the angels present.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended recitations
Note that Surah Ya-Sin is explicitly mentioned, and Surah al-Ra'd is added as a good practice (mustahabb). These surahs are recited in the presence of the dying person.
2
Determine the legal status of recitation
The recitation is not obligatory but recommended. The Hanafi school considers it sunnah or mustahabb. This is based on the wording 'yatluna' (they recite) and 'istahsana' (considered good).
3
Identify the dispute regarding removal
The text states 'they differed' (ikhtalafu) about removing a menstruating woman (ha'id), a postpartum woman (nafsa'), and a person in major impurity (junub). The disagreement is whether removal is required or recommended.
The basis for removal is that angels do not enter places where such individuals are present.
4
Understand the Hanafi position
The preferred Hanafi view is to remove these individuals out of respect for the angels, but it is not obligatory. If compassion or necessity dictates, they may remain.
Some scholars also recommend removing a disbeliever.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتلون عنده سورة يس واستحسن سورة الرعد واختلفوا في إخراج الحائض والنفساء من عنده، وكذا الجنب
They recite Surah Ya-Sin in his presence, and Surah al-Ra'd is considered good. And they differed regarding removing a menstruating woman and a postpartum woman from his presence, and similarly the one in a state of major impurity (junub).
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage continues the rulings for the dying person. It is recommended to recite Surah Ya-Sin, and some scholars also recommend Surah al-Ra'd. There is a difference of opinion about whether a woman in menstruation (ha’id) or postpartum (nafsa’) should be removed from the presence of the dying person, as angels do not enter a place where such women are present. The same applies to a person in a state of janabah. The preferred view is to remove them out of consideration for the angels, but if there is need or compassion, it may be overlooked. Some scholars also recommend removing a disbeliever.

Key Terms
الحائض (al-ha'id): A woman experiencing menstruation.
النفساء (al-nafsa'): A woman in the postpartum period after childbirth.
الجنب (al-junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Immediate Actions After Death: The First Rites
Rulings on binding jaw, closing eyes, placing iron, and hastening preparation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunnah and wajib actions immediately after death and identify which rulings apply to specific cases (child, menstruating woman, junub).

Core Idea
Tie the jaw, close the eyes, hasten preparation — death's arrival demands immediate, careful rites.

This lesson covers the first steps after death according to the Hanafi school. From the moment of death, specific actions become sunnah or wajib to prepare the body. The passage outlines the order: tying the jaw, closing the eyes with a supplication, placing iron, and hastening the washing. Understanding these rulings ensures the deceased is treated with dignity and the rites are performed correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify each action and its ruling
List each action mentioned (tie jaw, close eyes, place iron, etc.) and classify as sunnah, wajib, makruh, etc. For example, tying jaw is sunnah, placing hands on chest is not permissible, Quran recitation is makruh until after washing.
Use the key terms for precise Arabic terminology.
2
Note the exceptions
Who is exempt from wudu? A child who does not understand prayer, or a menstruating/postpartum woman. For a junub, include mouth and nose rinsing. Understand the rationale behind these exceptions.
The exceptions are based on the ritual purity state of the deceased.
3
Understand the sequence
The order matters: cover private parts, strip clothes, give wudu (if applicable), wipe head, wash with sidr. This sequence is part of the sunnah method of preparing the deceased.
The order is derived from the Prophet's practice.
4
Apply the rulings to a scenario
Given a specific deceased person (e.g., an adult male who died in a state of janaba), state each action and whether it applies. For example: 'Tie jaw (sunnah), close eyes (sunnah), give wudu with rinsing mouth and nose (because he was junub)...'
Practice synthesising the rulings from the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا مات شد لحياه وغمض عيناه، ويقول مغمضه: بسم الله وعلى ملة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اللهم يسر عليه أمره وسهل عليه ما بعده وأسعده بلقائك واجعل ما خرج إليه خيرا من الدار الأخرى عنه، وتوضع على بطنه حديدة لئلا ينتفخ، وتوضع يداه بجنبيه، ولا يجوز وضعهما على صدره، وتكره قراءة القرآن عنده حتى يغسل، ولا بأس بإعلام الناس بموته، ويعجل بتجهيزه، فيوضع كما مات على سرير مجمر وتراً ويوضع كيف اتفق على الأصح، ويستر عورته، ثم جرد عن ثيابه، ووضىء إلا أن يكون صغيرا لا يعقل الصلاة أو حائضاً أو نفساء، بلا مضمضة واستنشاق إلا أن يكون جنبا، ويمسح رأسه، وصب عليه ماء مغلى بسدر أو حرض
When he dies, his jaw is tied and his eyes are closed. The one closing his eyes says: 'In the name of Allah and upon the religion of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. O Allah, make his matter easy, make what follows easy for him, make him happy by meeting You, and make what he has gone to better for him than the other world.' An iron is placed on his belly so it does not swell. His hands are placed by his sides; it is not permissible to place them on his chest. Reciting Quran by him is disliked until he is washed. There is no harm in announcing his death to people. His preparation should be hastened. He is placed as he died on a bier with a censer an odd number of times, and he is placed however it happens on the soundest view. His private parts are covered. Then he is stripped of his clothes. He is given wudu unless he is a child who does not understand prayer, or a menstruating or postpartum woman, without rinsing the mouth and nose unless he is junub. His head is wiped. Boiling water with sidr or potash is poured over him.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage details the immediate actions after death. The jaw is tied with a bandage, eyes closed with a supplication. An iron piece is placed on the abdomen to prevent bloating. Hands are placed at sides, not on chest. Reciting Quran is disliked until after washing. Announcing death is allowed, even recommended to increase attendees. Preparation should be hastened. The deceased is placed on a bier and fumigated an odd number of times (3 or 5). Private parts from navel to knee must be covered. Clothes are removed. Wudu is performed without mouth and nose rinsing unless the deceased was junub. For children below understanding age or menstruating/postpartum women, wudu is not needed. Washing is done with water boiled with sidr (lote leaves) or potash (detergent).

Key Terms
شد اللحيين (shadd al-lahiyayn): Binding the jaw to prevent it from opening after death.
تغميض العينين (taghmeed al-'aynayn): Closing the eyes of the deceased.
المجمر (al-mijmar): A censer or incense burner used to fumigate the bier.
السدر (al-sidr): Lote tree leaves used in washing the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on reciting Quran by the deceased before washing?
A) It is recommended
B) It is obligatory
C) It is disliked (makruh)
D) It is prohibited (haram)

Key Takeaway
Immediately after death, perform the sunan of tying the jaw, closing the eyes, and hastening washing, while avoiding Quran recitation until after washing.

Husband's Obligation to Shroud His Wife: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the husband's duty to shroud his wife.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the husband's obligation to shroud his wife and explain why Abu Yusuf's view is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
The husband must shroud his wife absolutely, even if poor, according to the relied-upon position.

When a wife dies, who is responsible for her shrouding? This question generated an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf held the husband must pay absolutely, while Muhammad argued marriage severs all ties at death. The later tradition chose Abu Yusuf's view. This lesson examines the arguments and the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is 'tajhiz' (preparing) the deceased wife for burial. According to the mufta bihi, what is the hukm?
The hukm is wajib, not fard, because the dalil is considered zanni al-thubut.
2
State the opposing positions
What did Abu Yusuf hold? What did Muhammad al-Shaybani hold? Abu Yusuf: absolute obligation even if husband poor. Muhammad: no obligation.
3
Trace the basis of each position
For Muhammad, the dalil is 'inqita' al-zawjiyya min kulli wajh' (the marital relationship is severed from every aspect). For Abu Yusuf, no explicit dalil is given in the text; the ruling is based on continuation of certain spousal duties after death.
The text does not provide Abu Yusuf's proof; it declares his view as fatwa.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical consequence? Under Abu Yusuf, a poor husband must still pay; under Muhammad, he is not liable, shifting responsibility to the wife's estate or family.
This difference affects who bears the financial burden.
5
Note the tarjih and authority
The text says 'wa alayhi al-fatwa' (upon it is the fatwa) and cites that it is the choice of the authors of al-Mughni, al-Muhit, and al-Zahiriyya. This establishes the mufta bihi.
The authority weight is fatawa mutakhkhirin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بأس بتقبيل الميت، وعلى الرجل تجهيز امرأته، ولو معسرا في الأصح، ومن لا مال له فكفنه على من تلزمه نفقته، وإن لم يوجد من تجب عليه نفقته ففي بيت المال، فإن لم يعط عجزا أو ظلما فعلى الناس، ويسأل له التجهيز. وعلى الرجل إلخ: أي يجب على الرجل تكفين زوجتها ودفنها عند أبي يوسف لو كانت معسرة، وهذا التخصيص مختار صاحب "المغني" و"المحيط" و"الظهيرية"، ويُلزمه أبو يوسف بالتجهيز مطلقاً أي ولو كان الزوج معسراً وهي موسرة في الأصح، وعليه الفتوى، وقال محمد : ليس عليه تكفينها؛ لانقطاع الزوجية من كل وجه. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٧٣] لا مال له إلخ: قيد به؛ لأنه لو كان له مال فإنه يجب فيه، ويقدم على الدين والوصية والإرث إلى قدر السنة ما لم يتعلق بعين ماله حق الغير كالرهن والمبيع قبل القبض والعبد الجاني، وأراد بقوله: "من تلزمه": الذين هم ذوو رحم محرم من الميت نسبا، وإذا تعدد من وجبت عليه النفقة فالكفن على قدر ميراثهم كالنفقة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٧٤، حاشية الطحطاوي] بيت المال أي في بيت المال تكفينه وتجهيزه، أطلقه بأموال التركات التي لا وارث لأصحابها لا من غيرها كبيت الخراج والخمس والركاز، ولأحدهما الاستقراض من الآخر. [مراقي الفلاح والطحطاوي بتصرف: ٥٧٤] فإن إلخ: أي فإن لم يعط بيت المال؛ لكونه عاجزاً من تجهيز الميت؛ لخلوه من الأموال، أو لكون الأمير ظالماً يمنع صرف المال إلى مستحقيه، فيجب على من قدر عليه من الناس ويفترض على سائر ناس العالمين أن يجهزوه ويكفنوه. ويسأل له التجهيز [بالنصب] أي ويجب أن يسأل للميت التجهيز من لا يقدر عليه غيره من القادرين، بخلاف الحي إذا عري لا يجب السؤال له، بل يسأل بنفسه ثوباً لقدرته عليه، وإذا فضل عنه شيء صرف لمالكه، وإن لم يعرف كفن به آخر، وإلا تصدق به. [مراقي الفلاح بتصرف: ٥٧٤]
And there is no harm in kissing the deceased. And upon the man is the preparation of his wife, even if he is poor in the most correct view. And whoever has no wealth, his shroud is upon those whose maintenance is obligatory upon them. And if there is no one upon whom his maintenance is obligatory, then in the public treasury. And if it is not given due to inability or oppression, then upon the people, and one should ask for his preparation. Commentary on 'And upon the man etc.': i.e., it is obligatory upon the man to shroud his wife and bury her in the view of Abu Yusuf if she is poor. This specification is chosen by the author of al-Mughni, al-Muhit, and al-Zahiriyya. And Abu Yusuf obligates him to prepare absolutely, even if the husband is poor and she is wealthy in the most correct view, and upon it is the fatwa. And Muhammad said: he is not obligated to shroud her because the marital relationship is severed from every aspect. [Marqi al-Falah: 573] Commentary on 'whoever has no wealth etc.': it is restricted because if he has wealth, it is obligatory from it, and it takes precedence over debt, bequest, and inheritance up to the amount of the sunnah, unless there is a right of others attached to his property like a pledge, a sale before delivery, and a slave who has committed an offense. And by 'those upon whom' he means those who are mahram relatives of the deceased by lineage. And if there are multiple persons upon whom maintenance is obligatory, then the shroud is according to their shares of inheritance like maintenance. [Marqi al-Falah: 574, Hashiyah al-Tahtawi] Commentary on 'public treasury': i.e., in the public treasury, his shrouding and preparation. He said it absolutely with the wealth of estates that have no heir, not from other sources like the land tax, fifth, and treasure trove. And one of them may borrow from the other. [Marqi al-Falah and al-Tahtawi adapted: 574] Then 'if it is not given etc.' i.e., if the public treasury does not give because it is incapable of preparing the deceased due to lack of funds, or because the ruler is oppressive and prevents the disbursement of funds to those entitled, then it is obligatory upon those who are able from the people and it is an individual obligation upon all people of the world to prepare and shroud him. And one should ask for his preparation (with nasb as object of 'ask') i.e., it is obligatory to ask for the preparation of the deceased from those who know of him and are able to prepare him while others are not able. Contrary to the living person if he is naked, it is not obligatory to ask for him, rather he himself asks for a garment because he is capable of it. And if something remains of the shroud, it is returned to its owner, and if the owner is unknown, then another is shrouded with it, otherwise it is given in charity. [Marqi al-Falah adapted: 574]
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage covers several rulings on funeral expenses. First, it states there is no blame in kissing the deceased. Then it discusses the husband's obligation to shroud his wife. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf says the husband must shroud her absolutely (even if poor), and this is the mufta bihi. Muhammad says it is not obligatory because marriage ends completely at death. The text also explains the order of responsibility for a poor deceased: first from his own wealth, then from those whose maintenance is obligatory on him (mahram relatives, in proportion to their inheritance shares), then from the public treasury (from estates with no heir), and if the treasury fails, the obligation becomes fard kifaya on the Muslim community. It also mandates asking for the deceased's preparation from those able to provide, distinguishing this from a living person who can ask for himself. Any surplus shroud cloth is returned to the owner or used for another poor deceased.

Key Terms
تجهيز (tajhiz): Preparing the deceased for burial, including washing, shrouding, and burial
موسرة (muyassirah): A wealthy woman (opposite of poor)
معسر (mu'sir): A person in financial difficulty (poor)

Hierarchy of Responsibility for the Poor Deceased
Rulings on the sequence of responsibility for funeral expenses of a poor deceased.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the order of responsibility for shrouding a poor deceased and identify the conditions that trigger each level.

Core Idea
The shroud of a poor person comes first from his own wealth, then his maintenance obligors, then the bayt al-mal, then the community.

When a person dies with no wealth, who should cover the funeral expenses? The classical Hanafi rulings establish a cascading hierarchy: first the deceased's own property, then his relatives obligated for his maintenance (mahram), then the public treasury, and finally the Muslim community as a fard kifaya. This lesson unpacks each level and the conditions that move responsibility to the next.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial scenario
The passage begins with 'man la mala lahu' (whoever has no wealth). This is the starting point: the deceased is destitute.
2
First level: own wealth
If the deceased had any wealth, it must be used for his shroud, taking precedence over debts, bequests, and inheritance up to the sunnah amount, unless there are rights of others attached to his property.
This is a restriction: 'la mal lahu' means no wealth remains after these obligations.
3
Second level: maintenance obligors
If the deceased has no wealth, the shroud is upon those whose maintenance was obligatory on him (mahram relatives). If there are multiple, the cost is divided according to their inheritance shares, like maintenance.
The text specifies 'dhawu rahm mahram' (mahram relatives by lineage).
4
Third level: public treasury (bayt al-mal)
If no such relatives exist, the responsibility falls to the public treasury, funded specifically from estates with no heirs, not from other sources like kharaj, khums, or rikaz.
Bayt al-mal here is a fund for the indigent from heirless estates.
5
Fourth level: the Muslim community
If the treasury fails due to inability (lack of funds) or oppression (ruler refusing), the obligation becomes fard kifaya upon all Muslims who are able. It is also wajib to ask for the deceased's preparation from those capable.
This differs from a living person who can ask for himself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بأس بتقبيل الميت، وعلى الرجل تجهيز امرأته، ولو معسرا في الأصح، ومن لا مال له فكفنه على من تلزمه نفقته، وإن لم يوجد من تجب عليه نفقته ففي بيت المال، فإن لم يعط عجزا أو ظلما فعلى الناس، ويسأل له التجهيز. وعلى الرجل إلخ: أي يجب على الرجل تكفين زوجتها ودفنها عند أبي يوسف لو كانت معسرة، وهذا التخصيص مختار صاحب "المغني" و"المحيط" و"الظهيرية"، ويُلزمه أبو يوسف بالتجهيز مطلقاً أي ولو كان الزوج معسراً وهي موسرة في الأصح، وعليه الفتوى، وقال محمد : ليس عليه تكفينها؛ لانقطاع الزوجية من كل وجه. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٧٣] لا مال له إلخ: قيد به؛ لأنه لو كان له مال فإنه يجب فيه، ويقدم على الدين والوصية والإرث إلى قدر السنة ما لم يتعلق بعين ماله حق الغير كالرهن والمبيع قبل القبض والعبد الجاني، وأراد بقوله: "من تلزمه": الذين هم ذوو رحم محرم من الميت نسبا، وإذا تعدد من وجبت عليه النفقة فالكفن على قدر ميراثهم كالنفقة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٧٤، حاشية الطحطاوي] بيت المال أي في بيت المال تكفينه وتجهيزه، أطلقه بأموال التركات التي لا وارث لأصحابها لا من غيرها كبيت الخراج والخمس والركاز، ولأحدهما الاستقراض من الآخر. [مراقي الفلاح والطحطاوي بتصرف: ٥٧٤] فإن إلخ: أي فإن لم يعط بيت المال؛ لكونه عاجزاً من تجهيز الميت؛ لخلوه من الأموال، أو لكون الأمير ظالماً يمنع صرف المال إلى مستحقيه، فيجب على من قدر عليه من الناس ويفترض على سائر ناس العالمين أن يجهزوه ويكفنوه. ويسأل له التجهيز [بالنصب] أي ويجب أن يسأل للميت التجهيز من لا يقدر عليه غيره من القادرين، بخلاف الحي إذا عري لا يجب السؤال له، بل يسأل بنفسه ثوباً لقدرته عليه، وإذا فضل عنه شيء صرف لمالكه، وإن لم يعرف كفن به آخر، وإلا تصدق به. [مراقي الفلاح بتصرف: ٥٧٤]
And there is no harm in kissing the deceased. And upon the man is the preparation of his wife, even if he is poor in the most correct view. تكفين (takfin): Shrouding the deceased, i.e., wrapping in a burial shroud

The Shroud of a Man and Woman: Types and Specifications
Rulings on shroud levels and specifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah, kifayah, and darurah shrouds for a man and woman and identify which specifications are sunnah and which are obligatory.

Core Idea
The shroud must cover the body; the sunnah level is three pieces for a man and five for a woman, but the minimum is a wrapper and waist-wrapper plus a veil for a woman.

This lesson presents the Hanafi rulings on the shroud (kafan) – its types, number of pieces, and specifications according to sunnah, kifayah (sufficiency), and darurah (necessity). Understanding these distinctions ensures that the communal obligation of shrouding is fulfilled correctly, avoiding both deficiency and extravagance.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the three categories
The shroud is divided into three levels: sunnah (recommended), kifayah (sufficient), and darurah (necessity). Sunnah has the most pieces, kifayah is the minimum obligatory amount, darurah is whatever is available.
Sunnah is ideal, kifayah is mandatory, darurah is emergency.
2
Identify the pieces for a man
Sunnah: qamis (shirt from neck to feet without sleeves), izar (waist-wrapper), lifafah (wrapper covering head and feet). Kifayah: izar and lifafah. Darurah: any cloth that covers the body.
The qamis has no sleeves, armpit pieces, or collar.
3
Identify additional pieces for a woman
Sunnah adds a khimar (veil for face and head) and a khirqah (cloth to bind the breasts). Kifayah adds only the khimar. Darurah is the same as for men.
Hair is braided into two braids and placed on the chest.
4
Note key specifications and disliked items
The cloth should be white cotton. Wrapping is done left side first then right. Tying is only if needed. A turban is disliked for a man. Sleeves, collars, and folded edges are avoided.
These are sunnah; deviation does not invalidate the shroud.
5
Recognize the overall legal status
Shrouding the deceased is fard kifayah (communal obligation). The kifayah level is obligatory; omitting it without necessity is sinful. The sunnah level is meritorious but not required.
If the kifayah is not met, the shroud is invalid and must be rectified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكفن الرجل سنة قميص، وإزار ولفافة مما يلبسه في حياته، وكفاية: إزار ولفافة، وفضل البياض من القطن وكل من الإزار واللفافة من القرن إلى القدم، ولا يجعل لقميصه كم ولا دخريص ولا جيب ولا تكف أطرافه وتكره العمامة في الأصح ولف من يساره ثم يمينه، وعقد إن خيف انتشاره، واستحسنها بعضهم الكفن وتزاد المرأة في السنة خمارا لوجهها وخرقة لربط ثدييها، وفي الكفاية خمارا، أي وتزاد المرأة على ما ذكرناه للرجل ولو أمة ويجعل شعرها ضفيرتين على صدرها فوق القميص ثم الخمار فوقه تحت اللفافة، ثم الخرقة فوقها وتحمر الأكفان وترا قبل أن يدرج فيها، وكفن الضرورة ما يوجد. للرجل والمرأة جميعاً. وكفن الرجل : اعلم أن تكفين الميت فرض وأما عدد أثوابه فهي ثلاثة أقسام سنة وكفاية وضرورة كما بينها على التفصيل [مراقي الفلاح بزيادة: ٥٧٥] قميص وهو من أصل العنق إلى القدمين بلا دخريص وكمين. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٧٥] ولفافة وهي تزيد على ما فوق القرن والقدم ليلف فيها الميت وتربط من أعلاه وأسفله. [مراقي الفلاح بزيادة: ٥٧٥] مما يلبسه في حياته أي يؤخذ الكفن مما كان يلبسه الرجل في حياته يوم والعيدين. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٧٦] أفاد بطريق المنطوق جواز تكفينه في كل ما جاز لبسه وهو حي، من كل جنس، فيكفن بالبرد والقصب – بالتحريك ثياب ناعمة كتان من والكتان والقطن، ومنع بالمفهوم مالا يجوز لبسه في حال حياته كحرير ونحوه اعتباراً بحال الحياة، إلا إذا لم يوجد غيره، لكن لا يزاد على ثوب واحد؛ لأن الضرورة تندفع به ويجوز ذلك للنساء كمزعفر ومعصفر. [حاشية الطحطاوي بتغيير: ٥٧٦] وكفاية أي ما يكتفى به حال الاختيار بدون كراهة وهو القدر الواجب، وفي "الفتح" ويكره الاقتصار على ثوب واحد حالة الاختيار كما تكره الصلاة فيه حال الاختيار [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٧٦] كم بالضم مدخل اليد ومخرجها من الثوب. دخريص هو من القميص والدرع ما يوصل به البدن ليوسعه. ولا جيب هو النازل على الصدر. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٧٧] ولا تكف إلخ ولو كفت جاز بلا كراهة على الصحيح. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٧٧] ولف إلخ اقتصر المصنف على بيان لف الكفن والأصل: أن تبسط اللفافة، ثم الإزار فوقها، ثم يوضع الميت مقمّصا، ثم يعطف عليه الإزار ولف الإزار من جهة يساره، ثم من جهة يمينه ليكون اليمين أعلى، ثم فعل باللفافة كذلك اعتباراً بحالة الحياة. [مراقي الفلاح بزيادة: ٥٧٨] إن خيف إلخ أفاد بالشرط أنه إن لم يخف انتشار الكفن بأن كان المدفن قريباً لا يخشى انتشاره، فلا يعقد. وخرقة عرضها ما بين الثدي إلى السرة، وقيل: إلى الركبة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٧٨]
And the shroud of a man as sunnah is a shirt, a waist-wrapper, and a wrapper from what he used to wear in his life. And as sufficiency: a waist-wrapper and a wrapper. And the best is white from cotton. And each of the waist-wrapper and wrapper is from the crown to the foot. And one does not make for his shirt a sleeve, nor an armpit piece, nor a collar, nor does one fold its edges. And the turban is disliked in the most correct view. And one wraps from his left then his right, and ties if spreading is feared. And some considered it good (the turban). And the woman is increased in the sunnah a veil for her face and a cloth for binding her breasts. And in sufficiency, a veil. i.e., the woman is increased with what we mentioned for the man, even if she is a slave. And her hair is made into two braids on her chest above the shirt, then the veil above it under the wrapper, then the cloth above that. And the shrouds are dyed red? and odd in number before the deceased is wrapped in them. And the shroud of necessity is whatever is available. For man and woman alike. Commentary: And the shroud of a man: Know that shrouding the deceased is a fard. As for the number of its garments, they are three categories: sunnah, sufficiency, and necessity, as he explained in detail. [Marqi al-Falah with addition: 575] A shirt: from the base of the neck to the feet, without armpit piece and sleeves. [Marqi al-Falah: 575] A wrapper: it exceeds above the crown and below the foot to wrap the deceased and is tied at its top and bottom. [Marqi al-Falah with addition: 575] From what he used to wear in his life: i.e., the shroud is taken from what the man used to wear in his life on Fridays and Eid. [Marqi al-Falah: 576] He indicated by explicit meaning the permissibility of shrouding him in everything it was permissible for him to wear when alive, of any type. So he is shrouded in cold-weather garments and fine linen? and linen and cotton. And by implicit meaning, it forbids what is not permissible for him to wear in his life like silk and the like, considering the state of life, unless nothing else is found. But it should not exceed one garment because necessity is satisfied with that. And that is permissible for women, like safflower-dyed and saffron-dyed. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi amended: 576] And sufficiency: what suffices in a state of choice without dislike, and it is the obligatory amount. And in al-Fath, it is disliked to restrict to one garment in a state of choice just as it is disliked to pray in it in a state of choice. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 577] Sleeve: the entry and exit of the hand from the garment. 'Dukhris': in the shirt and armor, what connects to the body to widen it. No collar: it descends on the chest. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 577] 'And does not fold its edges': and if he folded, it is permissible without dislike based on the correct view. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 577] 'And wraps etc.': the author limited to explaining the wrapping of the shroud. The basic principle: spread the wrapper, then the waist-wrapper over it, then place the deceased wearing the shirt, then fold the waist-wrapper over him, wrapping from his left side then from his right side so that the right is on top, then do likewise with the wrapper, considering the state of life. [Marqi al-Falah with addition: 578] 'If spreading is feared etc.': he indicated by the condition that if there is no fear of the shroud spreading (e.g., because the grave is close and no spreading is feared), then it is not tied. And the cloth's width is from between the breasts to the navel, and it is said to the knee. [Marqi al-Falah: 578]

Commentary
This passage details the rules for the shroud (kafan) of a man and woman, covering three levels: sunnah (recommended), kifayah (sufficient/minimum required), and darurah (necessity). For a man, the sunnah shroud consists of three pieces: a shirt (qamis) covering from neck to foot without sleeves or armpit pieces, a waist-wrapper (izar) and a wrapper (lifafah) that extends beyond the head and feet. The kifayah level is two pieces: izar and lifafah. The darurah level is whatever cloth is available. The recommended material is white cotton. For a woman, the sunnah adds a veil (khimar) for the face and a cloth (khirqah) to bind the breasts; the kifayah adds only a veil. The hair is braided and placed on the chest. The wrapping method: spread the lifafah, then the izar, place the deceased in the shirt, then wrap the izar from left side first, then right, then similarly the lifafah. Tying the shroud is only done if there is fear of unravelling. The turban (amama) is disliked for men. Any surplus cloth from the shroud is to be returned to the owner or used for another poor deceased.

Key Terms
قميص (qamis): A shirt-like garment for the deceased, from neck to feet, without sleeves or armpit pieces
إزار (izar): A waist-wrapper, a rectangular cloth wrapped around the lower body
لفافة (lifafah): A wrapper that covers the entire body, extending beyond the head and feet, used to envelop the deceased
خمار (khimar): A veil for the woman's face and head
خرقة (khirqah): A cloth for binding the woman's breasts
عمامة (amamah): A turban; disliked for the deceased man
كفاية (kifayah): The minimal sufficient shroud (2 pieces for man, 3 for woman after adding khimar)
ضرورة (darurah): Necessity shroud: whatever cloth is available, even one piece

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Permissible and recommended
B) Permissible but disliked
C) Impermissible (haram)
D) Obligatory (fard)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires at least two pieces for a man's shroud and adds a veil for a woman; the sunnah includes additional pieces and specific specifications that avoid resemblance to regular clothing.

The Obligatory Shroud and Its Levels for Men
Ruling on obligatory shroud and its levels for men

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three levels of shroud for a man (sunnah, kifayah, darurah) and identify the pieces required in each level.

Core Idea
Shrouding the deceased is fard kifayah; the sunnah for a man is three pieces, the sufficient is two, and the necessary is one.

In this passage, the author explains that shrouding the dead is a communal obligation. He then categorizes the shroud into three levels: the complete sunnah, the sufficient amount without dislike, and the bare necessity. For a man, the sunnah consists of a shirt, a waist-wrapper, and an outer wrapper, with specific prohibitions on sleeves, gussets, and pockets. Understanding these levels helps ensure the deceased is honored appropriately.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligation level
The passage states 'اعلم أن تكفين الميت فرض' – know that shrouding the deceased is fard. This is a communal obligation (fard kifayah).
Fard kifayah means if some members perform it, others are absolved.
2
List the three categories of shroud
The text divides the shroud into three categories: sunnah (complete), kifayah (sufficiency), and darurah (necessity). Each has a different number of pieces.
The terms appear in the passage as 'سنة وكفاية وضرورة'.
3
Enumerate the sunnah pieces for a man
For a man, the sunnah shroud consists of three pieces: a shirt (qamis), a waist-wrapper (izar), and an outer wrapper (lifafah). The shirt must be from neck to feet without sleeves, gussets, or pockets.
The shirt is like a seamless garment; the izar covers from head to feet; the lifafah is longer to allow tying.
4
Understand the kifayah level
The kifayah (sufficient) level for a man is two pieces: izar and lifafah. This is the obligatory amount; it is disliked to use only one piece when more is available.
'وكفاية: إزار ولفافة' – sufficiency: a waist-wrapper and a wrapper.
5
Note the necessity level and additional rulings
In necessity (darurah), any cloth that covers the entire body suffices, even a single piece. Also, the turban is disliked in the correct view. Wrapping should start from the left side then the right.
The passage mentions the turban is disliked; some scholars considered it good, but the relied-upon position is dislike.

كتاب الصلاة ١٨٥ أحكام الجنائز من لا يقدر عليه غيره، وكفن الرجل سنة قميص ،وإزار ولفافة مما يلبسه في مفعول ثان لـ " يسأل" هو والدرع سواء من القرن إلى القدم حياته، وكفاية: إزار ولفافة، وفضل البياض من القطن وكل من الإزار واللفافة من القرن إلى القدم، ولا يجعل لقميصه كم ولا دخريص ولا جيب ولا تكف أطرافه وتكره العمامة في الأصح ولف من يساره ثم يمينه، وعقد إن خيف انتشاره، واستحسنها بعضهم الكفن وتزاد المرأة في السنة خمارا لوجهها وخرقة لربط ،ثدييها، وفي الكفاية خمارا، أي وتزاد المرأة على ما ذكرناه للرجل ولو أمة ويجعل شعرها ضفيرتين على صدرها فوق القميص ثم الخمار فوقه تحت اللفافة، ثم متعلق بمحذوف أي وتوضعان أي على رأسها ووجهها الخرقة فوقها وتحمر الأكفان وترا قبل أن يدرج فيها، وكفن الضرورة ما يوجد. للرجل والمرأة جميعاً الميت الجمعة وكفن الرجل : اعلم أن تكفين الميت ،فرض وأما عدد أثوابه فهي ثلاثة أقسام سنة وكفاية، وضرورة كما بينها على التفصيل مراقي الفلاح بزيادة ٥٧٥ قميص وهو من أصل العنق إلى القدمين بلا دخريص وكمين. مراقي الفلاح ٥٧٥] ولفافة وهي تزيد على ما فوق القرن والقدم ليلف فيها الميت وتربط من أعلاه وأسفله. مراقي الفلاح بزيادة: ٥٧٥] مما يلبسه في حياته أي يؤخذ الكفن مما كان يلبسه الرجل في حياته يوم والعيدين. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٧٦]، أفاد بطريق المنطوق جواز تكفينه في كل ما جاز لبسه وهو حي، من كل جنس، فيكفن بالبرد والقصب – بالتحريك ثياب ناعمة كتان من والكتان والقطن، ومنع بالمفهوم مالا يجوز لبسه في حال حياته كحرير ونحوه اعتباراً بحال الحياة، إلا إذا لم يوجد غيره، لكن لا يزاد على ثوب واحد؛ لأن الضرورة تندفع به ويجوز ذلك للنساء كمزعفر ومعصفر. [ حاشية الطحطاوي بتغيير: ٥٧٦] وكفاية أي ما يكتفى به حال الاختيار بدون كراهة وهو القدر الواجب، وفي "الفتح" : ويكره الاقتصار على ثوب واحد حالة الاختيار كما تكره الصلاة فيه حال الاختيار [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٧٦] كم بالضم مدخل اليد ومخرجها من الثوب. دخريص هو من القميص والدرع ما يوصل به البدن ليوسعه. ولا جيب: هو النازل على الصدر. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٧٧] ولا تكف إلخ ولو كفت جاز بلا كراهة على الصحيح. حاشية الطحطاوي : ٥٧٧] ولف إلخ اقتصر المصنف على بيان لف الكفن والأصل: أن تبسط اللفافة، ثم الإزار فوقها، ثم يوضع الميت مقمّصا، ثم يعطف عليه الإزار ولف الإزار من جهة يساره، ثم من جهة يمينه ليكون اليمين أعلى، ثم فعل باللفافة كذلك اعتباراً بحالة الحياة. [ مراقي الفلاح بزيادة: ٥٧٨] إن خيف إلخ: أفاد بالشرط أنه إن لم يخف انتشار الكفن بأن كان المدفن قريباً لا يخشى انتشاره، فلا يعقد. وخرقة عرضها ما بين الثدي إلى السرة، وقيل: إلى الركبة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٧٨] الشق
Book of Prayer 185. Rulings of Funerals. For one who has no one else to do it. The shroud of a man as sunnah is a shirt, a waist-wrapper, and a wrapper from what he wears in his life... Sufficiency: a waist-wrapper and a wrapper. The preferred white cotton. Each of the waist-wrapper and wrapper from the head to the feet. Do not make sleeves, gussets, or pockets for his shirt, and do not fold its edges. The turban is disliked in the correct view. Wrap from his left then his right, and tie if his unfolding is feared. Some considered it good. The shroud. The woman is given additionally in the sunnah a veil for her face and a cloth to tie her breasts. In sufficiency, a veil... The cloth of necessity is what is available. For the man and woman together... Know that shrouding the deceased is fard. As for the number of garments, they are three categories: sunnah, sufficiency, and necessity...
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi commentary explains the rulings of the shroud (kafan) for the deceased. It begins by stating that shrouding is a fard obligation. The shrouds are divided into three levels: sunnah (complete), sufficiency (adequate without dislike), and necessity (minimal). For a man, the sunnah consists of three pieces: a shirt (qamis), a waist-wrapper (izar), and a large wrapper (lifafah). The shirt should be from the neck to the feet without sleeves, gussets, or pockets. The waist-wrapper and wrapper should cover from head to toe. The turban is disliked. The binding should start from left then right, and knotting is only done if the shroud may loosen. For a woman, the sunnah adds a veil (khimar) for her face and a cloth to bind her breasts. Her hair is placed in two braids on her chest over the shirt, then the veil over that, under the wrapper. In sufficiency, a woman is given a veil. In necessity, any cloth suffices. The text also discusses that the shroud may be taken from the deceased's own clothes, and it is permissible to use any cloth he could wear while alive, but not silk or similar for men unless necessary. The commentary further explains technical terms like 'kumm' (sleeve), 'dakhris' (gusset), and 'jayb' (pocket).

Key Terms
كفن (kafan): The cloth(s) used to shroud the deceased body.
إزار (izar): A waist-wrapper from navel to feet, used as part of the shroud.
لفافة (lifafah): The large outer wrapper that covers the entire body, longer than the body to allow for tying.
قميص (qamis): A shirt-like garment from neck to feet without sleeves, gussets, or pockets.
عمامة (imamah): Turban; its use in the shroud is disliked according to the correct Hanafi view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the turban for a man's shroud according to the reliable Hanafi position?
A) It is sunnah
B) It is obligatory
C) It is disliked
D) It is forbidden

Key Takeaway
The shroud of a man should follow the sunnah of three pieces, but two suffice without dislike, and one is acceptable in necessity.

The Sunnah Shroud for Women and Additional Rulings
Ruling on sunnah shroud for women and dressing order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the additional pieces for a woman's shroud (veil and breast cloth) and explain the order of dressing and hair placement.

Core Idea
For a woman, the sunnah shroud adds a veil (khimar) and a breast cloth; her hair is braided and placed on her chest.

This passage continues with the specifics of a woman's shroud. In addition to the three pieces for a man, a woman is given a veil (khimar) to cover her face and a cloth (khirqah) to bind her breasts. The text also details the order of placing the cloths and how to arrange her hair in two braids on her chest. Understanding these details ensures the proper honor for a deceased woman.

Guided Path
1
Identify the additional pieces for a woman
The text says 'وتزاد المرأة في السنة خمارا لوجهها وخرقة لربط ثدييها' – the woman is given a veil for her face and a cloth to tie her breasts. These are in addition to the three pieces for a man.
The khimar covers the head and face; the khirqah binds the breasts.
2
Note the kifayah level for women
For sufficiency (kifayah), the woman is given a khimar in addition, as stated: 'وفي الكفاية خمارا'. This implies the izar and lifafah are still used, plus the khimar.
The text says 'وفي الكفاية خمارا' – and in sufficiency, a veil.
3
Learn the order of dressing
The order is: first the shirt (qamis), then the hair is placed in two braids on the chest over the shirt, then the khimar is placed over that, then the wrapper (lifafah) over everything.
The passage: 'ويجعل شعرها ضفيرتين على صدرها فوق القميص ثم الخمار فوقه تحت اللفافة'.
4
Understand the necessity level for women
The necessity (darurah) is the same as for men: any cloth that covers the entire body. The additional pieces are not required.
The text does not specify separate necessity for women; it implies the same rule.

Pillars and Conditions of the Funeral Prayer
Lists fard kifayah, pillars, and six conditions of funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two pillars and the six conditions of the funeral prayer, and apply the exceptions for riding and sitting.

Core Idea
The funeral prayer has two pillars and six conditions; ignoring any condition may invalidate the prayer.

The funeral prayer is a communal obligation. Its validity depends on specific pillars (arkan) and conditions (shurut). This passage from a Hanafi commentary lists these elements and discusses key exceptions, such as praying while riding or when the deceased is not on the ground.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal category
The passage begins by stating that the funeral prayer is fard kifayah. Understand what this means: if some perform it, the obligation is lifted from all.
فَرْض كِفَايَة
2
Distinguish pillars from conditions
The text first mentions the pillars (arkan) then the six conditions (shurut). Pillars are integral to the prayer; conditions are external prerequisites. Note that omitting a pillar invalidates the prayer, while a missing condition might be excusable in some cases.
أركان وشرائط
3
List the six conditions
Go through each condition: Islam of the deceased, purity of the deceased, purity of the shroud and place (with exceptions), the deceased placed in front, presence of the body (most or half with head), the prayer leader not riding without excuse, and the deceased on the ground unless excused.
See commentary for details
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi disagreement on sitting
The text mentions a difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (on one side) and Muhammad (on the other) regarding praying while sitting with an excuse. Determine the relied-upon position and understand the reasoning about the guardian's role.
عندهما لا عند محمد
5
Apply the conditions to a scenario
Given a scenario (e.g., deceased carried in hands), determine if the prayer is valid based on the conditions and exceptions discussed.
Practice applying conditions

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة ١٨٦ صلاة الجنازة فصل في صلاة الجنازة] الصلاة عليه فرض كفاية، وأركانها: التكبيرات، والقيام. وشرائطها ستة إسلام الميت وطهارته، وتقدمه وحضوره أو حضور أكثر بدنه أو نصفه مع رأسه وكون المصلي عليها غير راكب بلا عذر وكون الميت على الأرض وكذا غير قاعد فإن كان على دابة أو على أيدي الناس لم تجز الصلاة على المختار إلا من عذر. حكمية إسلام الميت : أطلقه فشمل ما إذا أسلم بنفسه أو بإسلام أحد أبويه أو بتبعية الدار ، وإذا استوصف البالغ الإسلام ولم يصفه ومات، لا يصلى عليه حاشية الطحطاوي بتغيير: ٥٨١] وطهارته : أي يشترط طهارته عن نجاسة وحقيقية في البدن، فلا تصح على من لم يغسل ولا على من عليه نجاسة، وهذا الشرط عند الإمكان، فلو دفن بلا غسل ولم يمكن إخراجه إلا بالنبش سقط الغسل وصلي على قبره بلا غسل للضرورة، بخلاف ما إذا لم يهل عليه التراب بعد فإنه يخرج ويغسل، ولو صلي عليه بلا غسل جهلاً أو نسياناً ثم دفن ولا يخرج إلا بالنبش، أعيدت على قبره استحساناً لفساد الأولى، ويشترط طهارة الكفن إلا إذا شق ذلك لما في "الخزانة": أنه إن تنجس الكفن بنجاسة الميت لا يضر دفعاً للحرج، بخلاف الكفن المتنجس ابتداءً [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٨١] ويشترط طهارة مكانه أيضا ؛ لأنه كالإمام. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٨١] وتقدمه الأولى تقديمه؛ لأن المخاطب به الأحياء وهم فاعلوا التقديم، فلو خلفهم لا تصح؛ لأنه كالإمام من وجه لا من كل وجه بدليل صحتها على الصبي [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٨٢] بلا عذر : أما بالعذر فتصح كما إذا كان مريضا ولو إماما فصلى قاعدا والناس خلفه قياما أجزأه عندهما لا عند محمد، بناء على الخلاف في صحة اقتداء القائم بالقاعد وعدمها، ولا فرق في المصلي قاعداً بعذر بين كونه ولياً أو لا؛ لأن كون الولي له حق التقدم لا يمنع سقوط الفرض بغيره ولو بدون إذنه، وإنما الولي له حق الإعادة، وحينئذ فلا فرق في سقوط الفرض بصلاة غير الولي بين أن يكون قائماً أو قاعداً لعذر. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٨٣] على الأرض: الظاهر أن اشتراط وضعه بالنسبة للمدرك الذي لم يفته شيء من التكبير خلف الإمام، أما المسبوق ففي كون الوضع شرطاً له ،خلاف، ولهذا قالوا: إذا رفعت قبل أن يقضي ما عليه من التكبير فإنه يأتي به ما لم يتباعد، وعلى المشهور أنه يأتي به تترى بلا دعاء إن خشي رفع الميت على الأعناق [حاشية الطحطاوي بحذف: ٥٨٣] عذر مثل أن يكون بالأرض وحل لا يتأتى وضع الميت عليها. [ حاشية الطحطاوي بتصرف: ٥٨٣] إلا من .
Book of Prayer 186. Funeral Prayer. Chapter on Funeral Prayer] Prayer upon him is a communal obligation. Its pillars: the takbirs and standing. Its conditions are six: Islam of the deceased, his purity, his being placed in front, his presence or presence of most of his body or half with his head, that the one praying upon him is not riding without excuse, and that the deceased is on the ground and likewise that he is not sitting. If he is on an animal or in people's hands, the prayer is not valid according to the chosen view except with an excuse...
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi commentary explains the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) in detail. It begins by stating that the funeral prayer is a communal obligation (fard kifayah). Its pillars (arkan) are two: the takbirs (specifically four according to Hanafis) and standing. Then it lists six conditions (shurut): 1) The deceased must be Muslim, including a child whose parent converted or who follows the dar. If an adult was asked about Islam and did not profess it, no prayer is held. 2) The deceased must be physically pure (ritually washed and free from impurity) and the shroud and place should be pure, with exceptions for difficulty. 3) The deceased must be placed in front of the imam and congregation. 4) The deceased or most of his body (or half with head) must be present. 5) The prayer leader must not be riding unless excused. 6) The deceased must be on the ground, not on an animal or carried in hands, unless there is an excuse like mud. The text also discusses exceptions: if buried without washing, prayer may be offered at the grave if exhumation is not possible; if one prays sitting due to illness, it is valid according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (but not according to Muhammad? Actually the text says 'عندهما لا عند محمد' meaning it is valid according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) but not according to Muhammad? Wait, it says 'أجزأه عندهما لا عند محمد' so it's valid according to the two but not according to Muhammad. And the later discussion indicates no difference between a guardian and others in this ruling. Also, the condition of the deceased being on the ground applies to the person who catches the prayer from the beginning; a latecomer may complete the takbirs even if the bier is lifted.

Key Terms
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): A communal obligation; if some perform it, the obligation is lifted from all.
أركان (arkan): Pillars of the prayer; their omission invalidates the prayer.
شرائط (shara'it): Conditions that must exist for the prayer to be valid.
عذر ('udhr): A legitimate excuse that permits relaxing a condition, such as illness or fear.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The deceased must be in a coffin
D) The deceased must be placed on the ground

Key Takeaway
The funeral prayer requires two pillars (takbirs and standing) and six conditions; exceptions exist for riding and sitting with excuses.

Conditions of the Funeral Prayer (Shurut Salat al-Janazah)
Lists six conditions for funeral prayer validity with hashiah commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six conditions for the validity of the funeral prayer and explain how each condition is determined according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The funeral prayer is valid only when the deceased is Muslim, pure, present in front, on the ground, and the imam is not riding.

The funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) is a communal obligation (fard kifayah) that requires specific conditions for its validity. This passage from Nur al-Idah enumerates six essential conditions and provides detailed rulings from the hashiah (commentary) on exceptions and nuances. Understanding these conditions prevents common errors and ensures the prayer is performed correctly, fulfilling the collective duty toward the deceased.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and pillars
The passage opens by stating that the funeral prayer is fard kifayah and its pillars are the four takbirs and standing (qiyam). Note that these are the core actions; conditions are separate.
Pillars invalidate the prayer if omitted; conditions must be present for validity.
2
List the six conditions
Extract the six conditions from the text: (1) Islam of the deceased, (2) purity of the deceased, (3) the body placed in front of the imam, (4) the body present (or most/half with head), (5) the imam not riding without excuse, (6) the body on the ground.
The text says 'six' explicitly; ensure you capture all.
3
Examine each condition with hashiah details
For each condition, read the hashiah expansions: Islam includes conversion by parent or abode; purity requires washing and clean shroud/place; forward placement is preferred; presence of major part; riding only allowed with excuse; ground condition may be waived for necessity.
Focus on the exceptions and practical applications mentioned.
4
Analyze the intra-madhhab dispute on the seated imam
The hashiah notes that if the imam prays seated due to illness, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani allow standing followers, while Imam Muhammad disallows it. Understand the basis of this difference.
This is a minor point; the mufta bihi is the permissibility view.
5
Apply the conditions to an exception case
Consider the case where the deceased is buried without washing. The text states that if exhuming is difficult, the washing is waived and prayer is performed on the grave. This shows how necessity overrides conditions.
This illustrates the principle of darurah (necessity) in Hanafi fiqh.
