[مراقي الفلاح: ٥٨١] وتقدمه الأولى تقديمه؛ لأن المخاطب به الأحياء وهم فاعلو التقديم، فلو خلفهم لا تصح؛ لأنه كالإمام من وجه لا من كل وجه بدليل صحتها على الصبي [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٨٢] بلا عذر : أما بالعذر فتصح كما إذا كان مريضا ولو إماما فصلى قاعدا والناس خلفه قياما أجزأه عندهما لا عند محمد، بناء على الخلاف في صحة اقتداء القائم بالقاعد وعدمها، ولا فرق في المصلي قاعداً بعذر بين كونه ولياً أو لا؛ لأن كون الولي له حق التقدم لا يمنع سقوط الفرض بغيره ولو بدون إذنه، وإنما الولي له حق الإعادة، وحينئذ فلا فرق في سقوط الفرض بصلاة غير الولي بين أن يكون قائماً أو قاعداً لعذر. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٨٣] على الأرض: الظاهر أن اشتراط وضعه بالنسبة للمدرك الذي لم يفته شيء من التكبير خلف الإمام، أما المسبوق ففي كون الوضع شرطاً له ،خلاف، ولهذا قالوا: إذا رفعت قبل أن يقضي ما عليه من التكبير فإنه يأتي به ما لم يتباعد، وعلى المشهور أنه يأتي به تترى بلا دعاء إن خشي رفع الميت على الأعناق [حاشية الطحطاوي بحذف: ٥٨٣] عذر مثل أن يكون بالأرض وحل لا يتأتى وضع الميت عليها. [ حاشية الطحطاوي بتصرف: ٥٨٣] إلا من عذر
The Book of Prayer, Chapter of Funeral Prayer, Section on Funeral Prayer: Prayer upon him is a collective obligation, and its pillars are the takbirs and standing. Its conditions are six: the deceased's Islam and purity, his being placed in front and present or most of his body or half with his head, the one praying being not riding without excuse, and the deceased being on the ground—similarly not seated, for if on an animal or in people's hands, the prayer is not permissible according to the chosen view except due to excuse. Ruling: Islam of the deceased: he made it absolute, so it includes if he became Muslim himself or by one of his parents becoming Muslim or by following the abode. If an adult is asked about Islam and does not describe it and dies, no prayer is performed upon him. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi modified: 581] And his purity: i.e., it is required that he be pure from physical impurity, so prayer is not valid upon one who has not been washed nor upon one upon whom there is impurity. This condition is when possible. If he was buried without washing and cannot be taken out except by digging, washing is waived and prayer is performed upon his grave without washing due to necessity, contrary to if soil has not been poured on him yet, then he is taken out and washed. If prayer was performed upon him without washing out of ignorance or forgetfulness, then he was buried and cannot be taken out except by digging, it is repeated upon his grave by istihsan because the first is invalid. Purity of the shroud is also required unless that is difficult, as in al-Khazanah: if the shroud becomes impure with the impurity of the deceased, it does not harm to avoid hardship, contrary to the shroud that became impure initially. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 581] Purity of the place is also required because it is like the imam. [Maraqi al-Falah: 581] His being placed in front: it is preferred to place him forward because those addressed are the living who perform the placing. If behind them, it is not valid because it is like the imam in one respect, not in all respects, as evidenced by its validity upon a boy. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 582] Without excuse: as for an excuse, it is valid, like if he is sick, even if he is the imam and prays seated while the people behind him are standing, it suffices according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], not according to Muhammad, based on the difference of opinion regarding the validity of the standing person following a seated person. There is no difference in the one praying seated due to excuse between being a guardian or not. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 583] On the ground: apparently the condition of placing him applies to the person who has not missed any takbir behind the imam. As for the latecomer, there is a difference regarding whether placing is a condition. Hence they said: if it is raised before he completes his takbirs, he performs them as long as not distant, and according to the well-known view he performs them successively without supplication if he fears the raising of the deceased on shoulders. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi with omission: 583] Excuse such as being in muddy ground where placing the deceased is not feasible. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi adapted: 583] Except due to excuse.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah presents the ruling and conditions of the funeral prayer. It begins by stating that the prayer upon a deceased Muslim is a fard kifayah (communal obligation), and its pillars (arkan) are the four takbirs and standing (qiyam). The author then lists six conditions: (1) the deceased must be Muslim, including those who became Muslim themselves or via a parent or by being in a Muslim abode; (2) the deceased must be pure from major and minor impurities, meaning the body must be washed and free from physical impurities; if washed and then buried, washing is waived if exhuming is difficult; (3) the deceased must be placed in front of the imam, because the living are the ones who place him; if the body is behind the congregation, prayer is invalid; (4) the body must be present, or at least the majority (half with the head); (5) the imam must not be riding without an excuse; if he prays seated due to illness, it is valid according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, but not according to Imam Muhammad's view; (6) the body must be on the ground or a similar surface, not on an animal or carried in hands, except for necessity. The hashiah adds details: for the condition of purity, if a shroud becomes impure from the deceased's own impurity, it is overlooked; the place must also be pure. Regarding forward placement, the condition is for those who catch all takbirs; a latecomer may pray even if the body is lifted. This section emphasises that funeral prayer is valid only when these conditions are met, following the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): A collective obligation: if some Muslims perform it, the rest are absolved.
التكبيرات (al-takbirat): The four takbirs said in the funeral prayer, considered pillars.
شرائط (shara'it): Conditions that must be fulfilled for the prayer to be valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The funeral prayer requires six specific conditions; neglecting any invalidates the prayer unless an excuse applies.

The Four Sunnah Acts of the Funeral Prayer
Enumerates four sunnah acts of janazah prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four sunnah acts of the janazah prayer and state the timing of each within the prayer.

Core Idea
The funeral prayer has four sunnah acts: standing location, praise, salawat, and supplication.

In this passage, the author enumerates the sunnah acts of the funeral prayer that complete its perfection. Understanding these sunnah acts is crucial for the imam and congregation to perform the prayer in the most complete manner. The sunnah acts are not obligatory but their omission reduces the reward.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four sunnah acts
The text lists four: qiyam opposite the chest of the deceased, thana after the first takbir, salawat after the second takbir, and du'a after the third takbir.
2
Note the position of each act
Each sunnah is tied to a specific takbir: after first takbir (thana), after second (salawat), after third (du'a). The fourth takbir is for salam.
3
Understand the ruling level
These are sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah). Omitting them does not invalidate the prayer but diminishes its perfection.
4
Distinguish from pillars
The takbirs themselves are pillars (arkan) of the janazah prayer; the sunnan are additional recommended acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسننها أربع قيام الإمام بحذاء صدر الميت ذكرا كان أو أنثى، والثناء بعد التكبيرة الأولى، والصلاة على النبي بعد الثانية والدعاء للميت بعد الثالثة، ولا يتعين له التكبيرة الثانية التكبيرة الثالثة شيء، وإن دعا بالمأثور فهو أحسن وأبلغ ومنه ما حفظ عوف من دعاء النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: " اللهم اغفر له وارحمه وعافه واعف عنه، وأكرم نزله ووسع مدخله، واغسله النزل: ما يهيأ للضيف قبره بالماء والثلج والبرد ونقه من الخطايا كما ينقى الثوب الأبيض من الدنس، وأبدله أمر من التنقية دارا خيرا من داره، وأهلا خيرا من أهله، وزوجا خيرا من زوجه، وأدخله الجنة، وأعذه من عذاب القبر وعذاب النار ، ويسلم بعد الرابعة من غير دعاء في ظاهر أي التكبيرة الرابعة الرواية، ولا يرفع يديه في غير التكبيرة الأولى، ولو كبر الإمام خمسا لم يتبع، ولكن ينتظر سلامه في المختار ولا يستغفر المجنون وصبي، ويقول: اللهم اجعله لنا فَرَطاً، واجعله لنا أجرا وذخرا واجعله لنا شافعا ومشفعا. ثواباً ذكرا كان أو أنثى فيه إشارة إلى أنه لا فرق فيما ذكر بين الصغير والكبير. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٨٣] له شيء: أي سوى كونه من أمور الآخرة مراقي الفلاح ٥٨٥] وعافه أمر . من المعافاة أي اجعله معافى من عذابك ونحوه واغسله بالماء: هذا كناية عن تطهيره من الذنوب بالكلية والإحسان إليه بما يذهب عنه هم الدنيا وما اقترفه فيها. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٨٥] في ظاهر الرواية استحسن بعض المشايخ أن يقول: ربنا آتنا في الدنيا حسنة إلخ، أو ربنا لا تزغ قلوبنا إلخ. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٨٦] في المختار: وفي رواية: يسلّم المأموم كما كبر إمامه الزائدة، ولو سلم الإمام بعد الثلاثة ناسياً كبر الرابعة ويسلم. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٨٧] المجنون قال البرهان الحلبي ينبغي أن يقيد بالأصلي؛ لأنه لم يكلف، بخلاف العارض فإنه قد كلّف، وعروض الجنون لا يمحو ما قبله، بل هو كسائر الأمراض. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٨٧] فَرَطاً: أي سابقاً مهيّنًا مصالحنا في الجنة، وهو دعاء للصبي بتقدمه في الخير. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٨٧] وذخراً بضم الذال المعجمة وسكون الخاء المعجمة : الذخيرة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٨٨] ومشفعا بفتح الفاء أي مقبول الشفاعة.
And its sunan are four: the imam standing alongside the chest of the deceased, male or female; praise (thana) after the first takbir; sending salawat upon the Prophet after the second; and supplication for the deceased after the third. Nothing specific is required for him in the second takbir or third takbir, and if he prays with the transmitted supplication, it is best and most effective. Among it is what 'Awf memorized from the supplication of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'O Allah, forgive him, have mercy on him, grant him well-being, pardon him, honor his lodging (i.e., what is prepared for a guest) and expand his entrance, wash his grave with water, snow, and hail, and purify him from sins as a white garment is cleansed from filth, and exchange his abode for a better one, his family for a better one, his spouse for a better one, admit him to Paradise, and protect him from the punishment of the grave and the Fire.' And he makes salam after the fourth without supplication in the apparent narration. He does not raise his hands except in the first takbir. If the imam does a fifth takbir, he is not followed, but he waits for his salam according to the chosen view. And one does not seek forgiveness for the insane person or a child. He says: 'O Allah, make him a precursor for us, a reward and a treasure, and make him an intercessor and one whose intercession is accepted.' Reward, male or female, it indicates that there is no difference in what is mentioned between the small and the large. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 583] 'Something specific': i.e., other than being matters of the Hereafter. [Maraqi al-Falah: 585] 'Grant him well-being' from al-mu'afah, i.e., make him free from Your punishment and the like. 'Wash him with water': this is a metaphor for purifying him from sins completely and bestowing goodness that removes worldly worries and what he committed. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 585] In the apparent narration, some scholars recommended saying 'Our Lord, give us in this world good...' or 'Our Lord, do not cause our hearts to deviate...' [Maraqi al-Falah: 586] In the chosen view: and in one narration, the follower makes salam as his imam made the additional takbir. If the imam made salam after three forgetfully, he does the fourth and makes salam. [Maraqi al-Falah: 587] Regarding the insane, al-Burhan al-Halabi said: it should be restricted to one born insane, because he is not obligated; otherwise, temporary insanity does not erase past obligation, it is like other illnesses. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 587] 'Faratan': i.e., preceding, preparing our benefits in Paradise; it is a supplication for the child to precede in goodness. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 587] 'Wa dhukhran' with a damma on the dhal and sukun on the kha: i.e., treasure. [Maraqi al-Falah: 588] 'Wa mushaffa'an' with a fatha on the fa: i.e., accepted intercession.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage details the sunnan (recommended acts) of the funeral prayer. There are four: (1) the imam stands directly opposite the chest of the deceased, whether male or female; (2) after the first takbir, he recites the thana (praise of Allah), similar to the opening supplication in regular prayer; (3) after the second takbir, he sends salawat upon the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him); (4) after the third takbir, he makes supplication for the deceased. The text emphasizes that no specific wording is obligatory; any supplication for the Hereafter is valid, but the best is the one transmitted from the Prophet (the du'a of 'Awf). After the fourth takbir, the imam says salam without any supplication, according to the apparent narration. Additional rulings: the imam does not raise his hands except for the first takbir; if the imam does a fifth takbir, the followers do not do it but wait for his salam; no istighfar is said for an insane person or a child; for a child, one says 'O Allah, make him a forerunner for us.' The hashiah clarifies that the insane person here refers to one born insane (not temporarily insane), and explains some terms of the supplication.

Key Terms
سنن (sunan): Recommended acts whose performance is meritorious but not obligatory; omission does not invalidate.
الثناء (al-thana): Praise and glorification of Allah, usually the du'a 'Subhanaka Allahumma...'
التكبيرة الأولى (al-takbirah al-ula): The first takbir (Allahu Akbar) with which the funeral prayer begins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Second takbir
C) Third takbir
D) Fourth takbir

Key Takeaway
The funeral prayer has four sunnah acts: imam opposite chest, thana, salawat, and du'a, each tied to a specific takbir.

Recommended Supplication and Additional Rulings in Funeral Prayer
Provides the transmitted du'a and additional rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recite the transmitted supplication for the deceased and apply the Hanafi rulings on raising hands, fifth takbir, and supplication for children and the insane.

Core Idea
The funeral prayer concludes with salam after the fourth takbir; hands are raised only at the first takbir.

After listing the sunnah acts, the author presents the recommended supplication transmitted from the Prophet and several practical rulings. These include the prohibition of supplication after the fourth takbir, the practice of raising hands only at the first takbir, the handling of a fifth takbir by the imam, and the specific supplication for a child. Understanding these details ensures the prayer is performed correctly according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Read the transmitted du'a
The text provides the du'a that 'Awf memorized from the Prophet. It is comprehensive and includes forgiveness, mercy, purification, and protection.
2
Note the ruling on salam
After the fourth takbir, the imam says salam without any supplication. This is the apparent narration.
3
Apply the ruling on raising hands
Hands are raised only at the first takbir, not at the others, according to the Hanafi school.
4
Handle the fifth takbir
If the imam performs a fifth takbir by mistake, the followers do not follow but wait for his salam.
5
Distinguish supplication for child and insane
For a child, one does not seek forgiveness but says 'Allahummaj'alhu lana faratan' (make him a forerunner). The insane person (born insane) is not prayed for with istighfar.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسننها أربع قيام الإمام بحذاء صدر الميت ذكرا كان أو أنثى، والثناء بعد التكبيرة الأولى، والصلاة على النبي بعد الثانية والدعاء للميت بعد الثالثة، ولا يتعين له التكبيرة الثانية التكبيرة الثالثة شيء، وإن دعا بالمأثور فهو أحسن وأبلغ ومنه ما حفظ عوف من دعاء النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: " اللهم اغفر له وارحمه وعافه واعف عنه، وأكرم نزله ووسع مدخله، واغسله النزل: ما يهيأ للضيف قبره بالماء والثلج والبرد ونقه من الخطايا كما ينقى الثوب الأبيض من الدنس، وأبدله أمر من التنقية دارا خيرا من داره، وأهلا خيرا من أهله، وزوجا خيرا من زوجه، وأدخله الجنة، وأعذه من عذاب القبر وعذاب النار ، ويسلم بعد الرابعة من غير دعاء في ظاهر أي التكبيرة الرابعة الرواية، ولا يرفع يديه في غير التكبيرة الأولى، ولو كبر الإمام خمسا لم يتبع، ولكن ينتظر سلامه في المختار ولا يستغفر المجنون وصبي، ويقول: اللهم اجعله لنا فَرَطاً، واجعله لنا أجرا وذخرا واجعله لنا شافعا ومشفعا. ثواباً ذكرا كان أو أنثى فيه إشارة إلى أنه لا فرق فيما ذكر بين الصغير والكبير. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٨٣] له شيء: أي سوى كونه من أمور الآخرة مراقي الفلاح ٥٨٥] وعافه أمر . من المعافاة أي اجعله معافى من عذابك ونحوه واغسله بالماء: هذا كناية عن تطهيره من الذنوب بالكلية والإحسان إليه بما يذهب عنه هم الدنيا وما اقترفه فيها. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٨٥] في ظاهر الرواية استحسن بعض المشايخ أن يقول: ربنا آتنا في الدنيا حسنة إلخ، أو ربنا لا تزغ قلوبنا إلخ. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٨٦] في المختار: وفي رواية: يسلّم المأموم كما كبر إمامه الزائدة، ولو سلم الإمام بعد الثلاثة ناسياً كبر الرابعة ويسلم. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٨٧] المجنون قال البرهان الحلبي ينبغي أن يقيد بالأصلي؛ لأنه لم يكلف، بخلاف العارض فإنه قد كلّف، وعروض الجنون لا يمحو ما قبله، بل هو كسائر الأمراض. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٨٧] فَرَطاً: أي سابقاً مهيّنًا مصالحنا في الجنة، وهو دعاء للصبي بتقدمه في الخير. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٨٧] وذخراً بضم الذال المعجمة وسكون الخاء المعجمة : الذخيرة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٨٨] ومشفعا بفتح الفاء أي مقبول الشفاعة.
And its sunan are four: the imam standing alongside the chest of the deceased, male or female; praise (thana) after the first takbir; sending salawat upon the Prophet after the second; and supplication for the deceased after the third. Nothing specific is required for him in the second takbir or third takbir, and if he prays with the transmitted supplication, it is best and most effective. Among it is what 'Awf memorized from the supplication of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'O Allah, forgive him, have mercy on him, grant him well-being, pardon him, honor his lodging (i.e., what is prepared for a guest) and expand his entrance, wash his grave with water, snow, and hail, and purify him from sins as a white garment is cleansed from filth, and exchange his abode for a better one, his family for a better one, his spouse for a better one, admit him to Paradise, and protect him from the punishment of the grave and the Fire.' And he makes salam after the fourth without supplication in the apparent narration. He does not raise his hands except in the first takbir. If the imam does a fifth takbir, he is not followed, but he waits for his salam according to the chosen view. And one does not seek forgiveness for the insane person or a child. He says: 'O Allah, make him a precursor for us, a reward and a treasure, and make him an intercessor and one whose intercession is accepted.' Reward, male or female, it indicates that there is no difference in what is mentioned between the small and the large. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 583] 'Something specific': i.e., other than being matters of the Hereafter. [Maraqi al-Falah: 585] 'Grant him well-being' from al-mu'afah, i.e., make him free from Your punishment and the like. 'Wash him with water': this is a metaphor for purifying him from sins completely and bestowing goodness that removes worldly worries and what he committed. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 585] In the apparent narration, some scholars recommended saying 'Our Lord, give us in this world good...' or 'Our Lord, do not cause our hearts to deviate...' [Maraqi al-Falah: 586] In the chosen view: and in one narration, the follower makes salam as his imam made the additional takbir. If the imam made salam after three forgetfully, he does the fourth and makes salam. [Maraqi al-Falah: 587] Regarding the insane, al-Burhan al-Halabi said: it should be restricted to one born insane, because he is not obligated; otherwise, temporary insanity does not erase past obligation, it is like other illnesses. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 587] 'Faratan': i.e., preceding, preparing our benefits in Paradise; it is a supplication for the child to precede in goodness. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 587] 'Wa dhukhran' with a damma on the dhal and sukun on the kha: i.e., treasure. [Maraqi al-Falah: 588] 'Wa mushaffa'an' with a fatha on the fa: i.e., accepted intercession.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage details the sunnan (recommended acts) of the funeral prayer. There are four: (1) the imam stands directly opposite the chest of the deceased, whether male or female; (2) after the first takbir, he recites the thana (praise of Allah), similar to the opening supplication in regular prayer; (3) after the second takbir, he sends salawat upon the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him); (4) after the third takbir, he makes supplication for the deceased. The text emphasizes that no specific wording is obligatory; any supplication for the Hereafter is valid, but the best is the one transmitted from the Prophet (the du'a of 'Awf). After the fourth takbir, the imam says salam without any supplication, according to the apparent narration. Additional rulings: the imam does not raise his hands except for the first takbir; if the imam does a fifth takbir, the followers do not do it but wait for his salam; no istighfar is said for an insane person or a child; for a child, one says 'O Allah, make him a forerunner for us.' The hashiah clarifies that the insane person here refers to one born insane (not temporarily insane), and explains some terms of the supplication.

Key Terms
فرط (farat): A forerunner; one who goes ahead to prepare benefits. In the supplication for a child, asking Allah to make the child a forerunner in Paradise.
شفع (shafa'a): Intercession. The phrase 'shafi'an wa mushaffa'an' means intercessor and one whose intercession is accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does the imam raise his hands in the funeral prayer?
A) At every takbir
B) Only at the first takbir
C) Only at the first and second takbir
D) Never

Key Takeaway
The funeral prayer has no supplication after the fourth takbir; hands are raised only at the first takbir; for a child, seek not forgiveness but a forerunner supplication.

Salah — Prayer

The Four Sunan of Janazah Prayer
Lists the four sunan and their supporting hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four sunnah acts of the funeral prayer and explain their legal status and evidence in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The funeral prayer has four recommended acts (sunan); omitting them does not invalidate the prayer but leaves it incomplete.

In this lesson, we examine the four sunan of the funeral prayer as established in the Hanafi school. These acts are recommended but not obligatory, and they are derived from the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him). We will also explore the preferred supplication and some related rulings, such as when to raise hands and how to handle a fifth takbir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four sunan
List each sunnah: standing opposite the chest, praising Allah after the first takbir, sending salawat after the second, and making du'a after the third.
The fourth sunnah is the du'a; no specific wording is obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of 'Awf ibn Malik is cited as evidence for the recommended supplication.
The hadith is a proof of desirability, not obligation.
3
Understand the Hanafi classification
These acts are sunnah muakkadah, meaning they are regularly performed by the Prophet and recommended but not fard or wajib.
Omitting them does not invalidate the prayer.
4
Note the exceptions and details
Hands are raised only in the first takbir; no du'a after the fourth takbir; for a child or insane person, a different supplication is said.
These details reflect the Hanafi position.
5
Apply: differentiate between sunnah and fard in practice
In a real scenario, ensure the four sunan are performed, but if one is missed, the prayer remains valid.
The sunan enhance the prayer's completeness.

[حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٨٣] له شيء: أي سوى كونه من أمور الآخرة مراقي الفلاح ٥٨٥] وعافه أمر . من المعافاة أي اجعله معافى من عذابك ونحوه واغسله بالماء: هذا كناية عن تطهيره من الذنوب بالكلية والإحسان إليه بما يذهب عنه هم الدنيا وما اقترفه فيها. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٨٥] في ظاهر الرواية استحسن بعض المشايخ أن يقول: ربنا آتنا في الدنيا حسنة إلخ، أو ربنا لا تزغ قلوبنا إلخ. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٨٦] في المختار: وفي رواية: يسلّم المأموم كما كبر إمامه الزائدة، ولو سلم الإمام بعد الثلاثة ناسياً كبر الرابعة ويسلم. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٨٧] المجنون قال البرهان الحلبي ينبغي أن يقيد بالأصلي؛ لأنه لم يكلف، بخلاف العارض فإنه قد كلّف، وعروض الجنون لا يمحو ما قبله، بل هو كسائر الأمراض. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٨٧] فَرَطاً: أي سابقاً مهيّنًا مصالحنا في الجنة، وهو دعاء للصبي بتقدمه في الخير. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٨٧] وذخراً بضم الذال المعجمة وسكون الخاء المعجمة : الذخيرة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٨٨] ومشفعا بفتح الفاء أي مقبول الشفاعة.
The funeral prayer: its sunan are four: the imam standing opposite the chest of the deceased, male or female; praise after the first takbir; sending salawat upon the Prophet after the second; and supplication for the deceased after the third. Nothing specific is determined for him (the imam), but if he supplicates with the reported (supplication) it is better and more eloquent. Among it is what 'Awf memorized from the supplication of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'O Allah, forgive him, have mercy on him, grant him well-being and pardon him, honor his place of rest, widen his entrance, wash him with water, snow, and hail, cleanse him from sins as a white garment is cleansed from filth, give him a house better than his house, a family better than his family, a spouse better than his spouse, admit him to Paradise, and protect him from the torment of the grave and the torment of the Fire.' He makes taslim after the fourth without supplication in the apparent narration. He does not raise his hands except in the first takbir. If the imam makes a fifth takbir, he is not followed, but rather he waits for his salam in the chosen view. No istighfar is made for the insane person or a child. And he says: 'O Allah, make him a forerunner for us, make him a reward and a treasure for us, and make him an intercessor and accepted intercessor for us.' Male or female—this indicates that there is no difference in what was mentioned between small and big. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 583] 'Nothing specific': i.e., other than it being among matters of the afterlife. [Maraqi al-Falah: 585] 'Grant him well-being' is a command from 'afiyah: make him free from Your punishment and the like. 'Wash him with water': this is a metaphor for completely purifying him from sins and treating him well by removing from him the worry of this world and what he committed in it. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 585] In the apparent narration, some mashayikh preferred that he say: 'Our Lord, give us in this world good...' etc., or 'Our Lord, do not let our hearts deviate...' etc. [Maraqi al-Falah: 586] In the chosen view: And in one narration, the follower makes salam just as his imam made the extra (takbir). If the imam made salam after three (takbirs) forgetfully, he makes the fourth takbir and makes salam. [Maraqi al-Falah: 587] 'The insane person' – al-Burhan al-Halabi said it should be restricted to the permanent insanity because he was not obligated, unlike the temporary insanity, for he was obligated, and temporary insanity does not erase what came before it; rather it is like other illnesses. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 587] 'A forerunner' i.e., a predecessor preparing our interests in Paradise, and it is a supplication for the child for his precedence in goodness. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 587] 'A treasure' (dhukhran): with dammah on the dhal and sukun on the kha, meaning stored reward. [Maraqi al-Falah: 588] 'Accepted intercessor' (mushaffa'an) with fatha on the fa, i.e., whose intercession is accepted.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage states the four sunnan (recommended acts) of the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) according to the Hanafi school. The four are: (1) the imam stands opposite the chest of the deceased, regardless of gender; (2) praise (thana') after the first takbir; (3) salawat upon the Prophet after the second takbir; and (4) supplication (du'a) for the deceased after the third takbir. The text then emphasizes that no specific du'a is obligatory, but the one reported from the Prophet (the hadith of 'Awf ibn Malik) is best. This du'a includes asking for forgiveness, mercy, and entry into Paradise. The passage also clarifies the position on raising hands: only in the first takbir. If the imam makes a fifth takbir, the follower should not follow but wait for the imam's salam. No istighfar is made for an insane person or a child; instead, a different supplication is said. The marginal notes from al-Tahtawi and Maraqi al-Falah provide further lexical and legal clarifications, such as that 'nothing specific' means only matters of the afterlife are intended, and that the washing metaphor refers to complete purification from sins.

Key Terms
صلاة الجنازة (salat al-janazah): The funeral prayer performed over a deceased Muslim, consisting of four takbirs with standing and supplications.
سنن (sunan): Recommended acts in the funeral prayer that are not fard or wajib; omitting them does not invalidate the prayer but leaves it incomplete.
التكبيرة (al-takbirah): The utterance of 'Allahu Akbar' which marks each of the four parts of the funeral prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Raising hands in every takbir
B) Raising hands only in the first takbir
C) Raising hands only in the third takbir
D) Not raising hands at all

Key Takeaway
The four sunan of the funeral prayer are recommended acts derived from the Prophet's practice, and their omission does not affect the validity of the prayer.

Hierarchy for Leading the Funeral Prayer: The Base Order and an Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Establishes the hierarchy of who has right to lead funeral prayer and discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchy for leading the funeral prayer and explain the intra-madhhab dispute regarding the order and its harmonization.

Core Idea
The right to lead funeral prayer follows a fixed hierarchy; an alternative narration from Abu Hanifa reorders it, and scholars harmonize by interpreting key terms.

This passage from Nur al-Idah establishes who has the primary right to lead the funeral prayer (imanah al-janazah). It presents a five-tier hierarchy: sultan, deputy, judge, imam of locality, guardian. However, an alternative narration from Abu Hanifa via Hasan ibn Ziyad presents a different order, and many later scholars adopted it. Understanding this dispute is key to applying the correct ruling in different contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base hierarchy
List the five persons in order from the matn: sultan, deputy, judge, imam of locality, guardian.
This order is the starting point.
2
Recognize the alternative narration
Note that Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated a different order from Abu Hanifa: supreme imam, city imam, judge, police chief, locality imam, nearest relative.
This adds the police chief and drops the deputy.
3
Understand the harmonization
See how the commentator reconciles: 'sultan' may refer to the supreme imam if present, or the city imam if not, aligning with the alternative order.
Thus the matn's 'sultan' is interpreted broadly.
4
Apply the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is the order of the matn, but many scholars adopt the narrated order; know which to follow in fatwa.
Local practice may vary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في بيان أحق الناس بالصلاة عليه ] السلطان أحق بصلاته ثم نائبه ثم القاضي، ثم إمام الحي، ثم الولي، ولمن له حق أي الخليفة التقدم أن يأذن لغيره، فإن صلى غيره أعادها إن شاء، ولا يعيد معه من صلى مع فالإعادة ليست بواجبة فاعل "لا يعيد" غيره، ومن له ولاية التقدم فيها أحق ممن أوصى له الميت بالصلاة عليه على المفتى به، وإن دفن بلا صلاة صلي على قبره السلطان أحق إلخ روى الحسن بن زياد عن أبي حنيفة أن الإمام الأعظم - وهو الخليفة – أولى إن حضر، وإن لم يحضر فإمام المصر أولى إن حضر ، فإن لم يحضر فالقاضي أولى فإن لم يحضر فصاحب الشرطة أولى، فإن لم يحضر فإمام الحي، فإن لم يحضر فالأقرب من ذوي ،قرابته وبهذه الرواية أخذ كثير من مشايخنا، وقوله في الكتاب: "السلطان": يجوز أن يراد به الإمام الأعظم إن حضر، فإن لم يحضر فإمام المصر. [العناية: ۸۱/۲] ثم إمام الحي: المراد به إمام مسجد محلته، لكن بشرط أن يكون أفضل من الولي وإلا فالولي أولى منه حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٨٩] ثم الولي: أي الولي الذكر المكلف، فلا حق للمرأة والصغير والمعتوه ويقدم الأقرب فالأقرب كترتيبهم في النكاح، ولكن يقدم الأب على الابن في قول الكل. [ مراقي الفلاح (٥۸۹] ولمن له حق إلخ أي يجوز لمن له حق التقدم الإذن للإمامة في صلاة الجنازة لغيره، وكذا له أن يأذن في الانصراف بعدها قبل الدفن؛ إذ هو بدون الإذن مكروه، أفاده السيد وفي سكب" الأنهر": لو انصرف بدون إذن الولي قيل يكره، وقيل: لا، وهو الأوجه [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٩٠] أعادها : أطلقه وهو مقيد بما إذا لم يأذن له ولم يقتد به الولي، أما إذا أذن له، أو لم يأذن ولكن صلى خلفه، فليس له أن يعيد؛ لأنه سقط حقه بالإذن أو بالصلاة مرة وهي لا تتكرر، ولو صلى عليه الولي وللميت أولياء آخرون بمنزلته ليس لهم أن يعيدوا؛ لأن ولاية الذي صلى متكاملة، وأفاد أن للولي حق الإعادة ولو على قبر الميت. [حاشية الطحطاوي بزيادة: ٥٩١] أحق ممن إلخ لأن الوصية باطلة على المفتى به، قاله الصدر الشهيد، وفي "نوادر" ابن رستم : الوصية جائزة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٩١] صلي على قبره: قال في "الفتح": هذا إذا أهيل عليه التراب؛ لأنه صار مسلما لمالكه تعالى، وخرج عن أيدينا، فلا يتعرض له، بخلاف ما إذا لم يُهل عليه فإنه يخرج ويصلى عليه، لكن في "الخلاصة" . عن "الجامع الصغير" للحاكم عبد الرحمن: ولو دفن قبل الغسل أو قبل الصلاة لا ينبش فإن دفنوه و لم يهيلوا عليه حتى علموا أنه لم يغسل لكنهم سووا اللبن، لا ينبش أيضاً، أي ويصلى على قبره ثانياً إذا صلى عليه أولاً [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٩١]
Chapter on explaining who is most entitled to pray over him: The sultan is most entitled to his prayer, then his deputy, then the judge, then the imam of the locality, then the guardian (wali). And whoever has the right (i.e., the caliph) to lead may authorize someone else. If someone else prays (without authorization), he (the one with right) may repeat it if he wishes. But the one who prayed with that other person does not repeat it; the repetition is not obligatory. And whoever has the authority to lead is more entitled than one whom the deceased appointed in his will to pray over him, according to the mufta bihi (relied-upon position). And if he is buried without prayer, prayer is performed over his grave. The sultan is most entitled, etc. – Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Abu Hanifa that the supreme imam (i.e., the caliph) is most entitled if present; if not present, then the imam of the city is most entitled if present; if not present, then the judge is most entitled; if not present, then the chief of police is most entitled; if not present, then the imam of the locality; if not present, then the nearest of his relatives. Many of our mashayikh adopted this narration. And what is in the book (the matn) 'the sultan' – it may mean the supreme imam if present, otherwise the imam of the city. [Al-Inayah 2/81] Then 'imam of the locality' – meaning the imam of the mosque of his neighborhood, but on condition that he be more virtuous than the guardian; otherwise the guardian is more entitled. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 589] Then 'the guardian' – meaning the male, legally responsible guardian; so the woman, minor, and insane person have no right. And the closest is given precedence over the next closest, like their order in marriage. But the father is given precedence over the son according to all. [Maraqi al-Falah: 589] 'And whoever has the right etc.' – meaning it is permissible for the one who has the right to lead to authorize someone else to lead the funeral prayer, and likewise he may authorize departure after it before burial; for without such authorization it is disliked. This was communicated by al-Sayyid. And in Sabk al-Anhar: if someone departs without the guardian's permission, it is said to be disliked, and it is said no, and this is more likely. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 590] 'He repeats it' – this is unrestricted but is restricted to when the guardian did not authorize and did not follow him. If he authorized him, or did not authorize but prayed behind him, then he has no right to repeat it, because his right has lapsed by authorization or by praying once, and it is not repeated. And if the guardian prayed over him and there are other guardians of equal status, they do not have the right to repeat, because the authority of the one who prayed is complete. And it is stated that the guardian has the right to repeat even over the grave of the deceased. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi with addition: 591] 'More entitled than one whom the deceased appointed...' because the will is invalid according to the mufta bihi, as said by al-Sadr al-Shahid. And in the Nawadir of Ibn Rustam, the will is permissible. [Maraqi al-Falah: 591] 'Prayer is performed over his grave' – he said in al-Fath: this is when soil has been thrown over him, because then he has become surrendered to his Owner, the Exalted, and has left our hands, so he is not disturbed. Unlike if soil has not been thrown, then he is taken out and prayer is performed. But in al-Khulasa from al-Jami' al-Saghir of al-Hakim Abd al-Rahman: if he was buried before washing or before prayer, he is not exhumed. If they buried him and did not throw soil over him until they knew he had not been washed, but they arranged the bricks, he is also not exhumed. i.e., and prayer is performed over his grave a second time if it had been prayed over once. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 591]
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage (a fasl from Nur al-Idah) outlines the hierarchy of who has the primary right (ahqaq) to lead the funeral prayer. The order is: (1) the sultan (ruler), (2) his deputy, (3) the judge, (4) the imam of the locality (imam al-hayy), and (5) the guardian (wali). The text then discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute: Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad narrates from Abu Hanifa a different order: the supreme imam (caliph) if present, then imam of the city, then judge, then chief of police, then imam of the locality, then nearest relative. Many Hanafi scholars adopted this narration. The author reconciles by interpreting 'sultan' as the supreme imam if present, otherwise the imam of the city. The passage also rules that the guardian may authorize someone else to lead; if someone prays without authorization, the guardian may repeat the prayer (but it is not obligatory). A key point: a bequest (wasiyyah) by the deceased appointing an imam is invalid according to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi), though there is a contrary narration from Ibn Rustam. Finally, if a person is buried without prayer, prayer is performed over the grave, provided soil has been thrown (to avoid disturbing the grave).

Key Terms
الولي (al-wali): The male, legally responsible guardian of the deceased, responsible for arranging the funeral; the father is given precedence over the son.
المفتى به (al-mufta bihi): The relied-upon legal position for issuing fatwa, here that a bequest appointing an imam is invalid.
السلطان (al-sultan): The ruler or highest political authority; in the context of funeral prayer, interpreted as the supreme imam (caliph) or city imam.
إمام الحي (imam al-hayy): The imam of the local neighborhood mosque.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi mufta bihi, if the sultan is absent, who leads the funeral prayer?
A) The deputy
B) The judge
C) The imam of the locality
D) The guardian

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi hierarchy for leading funeral prayer is subject to an intra-madhhab dispute, harmonized by interpreting 'sultan' broadly, and the relied-upon position follows the matn order.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Delegation, Repetition, Bequest Invalidity, and Grave Prayer
Explains delegation, repetition of prayer, invalidity of bequest, and grave-side prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rules regarding delegation of the funeral prayer, the right to repeat it, the invalidity of a bequest appointing an imam, and the permissibility of praying over the grave.

Core Idea
The one with right may delegate; unauthorized prayer may be repeated; a bequest is invalid; burial without prayer leads to grave-side prayer.

Beyond establishing the hierarchy for leading the funeral prayer, this passage addresses several practical issues that frequently arise. The right holder may authorize another to lead or to depart; if someone prays without authorization, the right holder may repeat the prayer; a bequest by the deceased appointing an imam is invalid according to the mufta bihi; and if a person is buried without prayer, prayer may be performed over the grave under specific conditions. These rulings ensure proper respect for the right holder and maintain the integrity of the funeral.

Guided Path
1
Understand delegation
The one with right (e.g., guardian) may authorize another to lead or to leave after prayer. Without authorization, departure is disliked.
Authorization can be explicit or implied by following the prayer.
2
Analyze repetition
If someone prays without authorization, the right holder may repeat the prayer, but only if he did not authorize and did not follow. If he authorized or followed, he cannot repeat because his right lapses.
The repetition is over the grave if already buried.
3
Examine bequest invalidity
A will appointing an imam is invalid according to the mufta bihi; the right holder takes precedence regardless. Note the contrary narration from Ibn Rustam.
This emphasizes that funeral prayer right is a shar'i right, not subject to the deceased's wishes.
4
Apply grave prayer rule
If buried without prayer, prayer over the grave is performed, but only after soil has been thrown (to avoid disturbing the grave). If before soil thrown, exhumation is possible but not recommended.
This shows care for the deceased's body and the grave's sanctity.

Priority of Leaders for Funeral Prayer
Ruling on who is most entitled to lead funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchy of entitlement to lead the funeral prayer and identify the conditions for the guardian (wali) to lead.

Core Idea
The ruler has the highest right to lead funeral prayer; the guardian only leads when no higher authority is present.

This lesson establishes the order of priority for who should lead the janazah prayer in the Hanafi school. While the prayer itself can be led by any qualified Muslim, the school gives precedence to certain individuals to uphold the dignity of the deceased and the community. We will examine the basic hierarchy from the matn and the expanded narration from Imam Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hierarchy as per the matn
List the five categories in order: sultan, his deputy, judge, imam of the neighborhood, guardian. Understand that each is entitled only if the previous is absent.
The matn is concise; the commentary clarifies each term.
2
Understand the alternative narration
Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Abu Hanifa a different order: caliph, city imam, judge, police chief, neighborhood imam, closest relative. Note that many Hanafi scholars preferred this narration.
This shows an intra-madhhab difference.
3
Analyze the condition for the imam of the neighborhood
The imam al-hayy is only entitled if he is more virtuous (afdal) than the guardian; otherwise the guardian takes precedence.
This condition is from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi.
4
Define the guardian (wali)
The guardian must be a male who is legally responsible (mukallaf). Women, minors, and the insane have no right. Among guardians, priority goes to the closest relative, similar to marriage order, but the father is always ahead of the son by consensus.
This definition is from Maraqi al-Falah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في بيان أحق الناس بالصلاة عليه السلطان أحق بصلاته ثم نائبه ثم القاضي ثم إمام الحي ثم الولي السلطان أحق إلخ روى الحسن بن زياد عن أبي حنيفة أن الإمام الأعظم - وهو الخليفة – أولى إن حضر، وإن لم يحضر فإمام المصر أولى إن حضر ، فإن لم يحضر فالقاضي أولى فإن لم يحضر فصاحب الشرطة أولى، فإن لم يحضر فإمام الحي، فإن لم يحضر فالأقرب من ذوي قرابته وبهذه الرواية أخذ كثير من مشايخنا، وقوله في الكتاب: "السلطان": يجوز أن يراد به الإمام الأعظم إن حضر، فإن لم يحضر فإمام المصر. [العناية: ۸۱/۲] ثم إمام الحي: المراد به إمام مسجد محلته، لكن بشرط أن يكون أفضل من الولي وإلا فالولي أولى منه [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٨٩] ثم الولي: أي الولي الذكر المكلف، فلا حق للمرأة والصغير والمعتوه ويقدم الأقرب فالأقرب كترتيبهم في النكاح، ولكن يقدم الأب على الابن في قول الكل. [مراقي الفلاح (٥۸۹]
A section explaining who is most entitled to pray over the deceased: The sultan is most entitled to his prayer, then his deputy, then the judge, then the imam of the neighborhood, then the guardian. The sultan etc.: Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Abu Hanifah that the greatest imam – and he is the caliph – is most entitled if present, and if not present then the imam of the city is most entitled if present, if not present then the judge is most entitled, if not present then the head of police is most entitled, if not present then the imam of the neighborhood, if not present then the closest of his relatives. Many of our scholars adopted this narration. His saying in the book: 'the sultan' may mean the greatest imam if present, if not present then the imam of the city. [al-`Inayah 2:81] Then the imam of the neighborhood: meaning the imam of his district's mosque, but on condition that he be better than the guardian; otherwise the guardian is more entitled than him. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi p.589] Then the guardian: meaning the male, legally responsible guardian. Thus no right for a woman, a minor, or an insane person. The closest is given precedence, like their order in marriage, but the father is preferred over the son according to all [scholars]. [Maraqi al-Falah p.589]
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement explaining the hierarchy of who has the right to lead the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) in the Hanafi school. The ruling as stated in the matn is: the sultan (ruler) is most entitled, then his deputy, then the judge, then the local imam, then the guardian (wali). The commentary then expands on this by providing an alternative narration from Imam Muhammad through Hasan ibn Ziyad that gives a slightly different order: first the caliph, then city imam, then judge, then police chief, then neighborhood imam, then closest relative. Many Hanafi scholars preferred this narration. The commentator clarifies that 'sultan' in the matn can refer to the caliph when present, otherwise the city imam. The 'imam of the neighborhood' is the imam of the local mosque, but only if he is more virtuous than the guardian; otherwise the guardian takes precedence. The 'guardian' is defined as a male who is legally responsible (mukallaf), so women, minors, and the insane have no right. Among guardians, the closest relative is prioritized, similar to priority in marriage, except that the father is always preferred over the son by consensus.

Key Terms
الولي (al-wali): The male, legally responsible guardian of the deceased who has the right to lead or authorize the funeral prayer
إمام الحي (imam al-hayy): The imam of the neighborhood mosque

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The judge
B) The sultan's deputy
C) The imam of the neighborhood
D) The guardian

Key Takeaway
The ruler holds the highest right to lead janazah; the guardian leads only when no higher authority is present and if he is a virtuous male.

Delegation and Repetition of Janazah Prayer
Ruling on permission to delegate and repetition of janazah prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which the guardian may repeat the janazah prayer and apply them to a given scenario.

Core Idea
The guardian may repeat the janazah prayer only if he did not give permission and did not follow the unauthorized imam.

The janazah prayer is led by the one most entitled, typically the guardian or caliph. However, he may delegate this right to another. This lesson examines what happens if someone else leads without permission: who may repeat the prayer and under what conditions? Understanding these rules ensures proper respect for the right of precedence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rightful Leader
Determine who has the right of precedence (e.g., the caliph, guardian of the deceased). This person is the default imam for the janazah prayer.
2
Analyze Delegation
Check if the rightful leader gave permission for another to lead. If he gave explicit permission, he loses the right to repeat.
Permission can be explicit or implicit by following the prayer.
3
Check Participation
Determine whether the rightful leader followed the prayer led by the other. If he prayed behind the unauthorized imam, he cannot repeat.
4
Conclude on Repetition
If the rightful leader neither gave permission nor followed, he may repeat the janazah prayer if he wishes. Those who prayed with the unauthorized imam do not need to repeat.
Repetition is permissible (ja'iz), not wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولمن له حق أي الخليفة التقدم أن يأذن لغيره، فإن صلى غيره أعادها إن شاء، ولا يعيد معه من صلى معه فالإعادة ليست بواجبة ولمن له حق إلخ أي يجوز لمن له حق التقدم الإذن للإمامة في صلاة الجنازة لغيره، وكذا له أن يأذن في الانصراف بعدها قبل الدفن؛ إذ هو بدون الإذن مكروه، أفاده السيد وفي سكب الأنهر: لو انصرف بدون إذن الولي قيل يكره، وقيل: لا، وهو الأوجه [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٩٠] أعادها: أطلقه وهو مقيد بما إذا لم يأذن له ولم يقتد به الولي، أما إذا أذن له، أو لم يأذن ولكن صلى خلفه، فليس له أن يعيد؛ لأنه سقط حقه بالإذن أو بالصلاة مرة وهي لا تتكرر، ولو صلى عليه الولي وللميت أولياء آخرون بمنزلته ليس لهم أن يعيدوا؛ لأن ولاية الذي صلى متكاملة، وأفاد أن للولي حق الإعادة ولو على قبر الميت. [حاشية الطحطاوي بزيادة: ٥٩١]
And for the one who has the right of precedence, i.e., the caliph, to give permission to someone else. If someone else prays, he may repeat it if he wishes, but those who prayed with him do not repeat it; the repetition is not obligatory. 'And for the one who has the right etc.' means: It is permissible for the one who has the right of precedence to give permission for another to lead the funeral prayer, and similarly he may give permission for departure after it before burial; since without permission it is disliked. The sayyid said: In Sabk al-Anhar, if one departs without the permission of the guardian, it is said to be disliked, and it is said not, and that is more appropriate. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi p.590] 'He may repeat it': this is unrestricted but restricted to when he did not give permission and the guardian did not follow him. If he gave permission, or did not give permission but he prayed behind him, then he may not repeat; because his right dropped by permission or by praying once, and it is not repeated. If the guardian prayed over him and the deceased has other guardians of the same rank, they may not repeat; because the guardianship of the one who prayed is complete. And it indicates that the guardian has the right of repetition even at the grave of the deceased. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi with addition p.591]
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage rules on the delegation of leading the janazah prayer. The one who has the right (e.g., the caliph or guardian) may permit another to lead. If someone else leads without permission, the one entitled may repeat the prayer, but those who prayed with the unauthorized imam are not required to repeat it. The commentary qualifies this: the right to repeat exists only if the entitled person did not give permission and did not follow the prayer. If he gave permission or prayed behind the other, he loses the right. Also, if there are multiple guardians of equal rank and one prays, others cannot repeat. Interestingly, the right to repeat is stated even at the grave (if already buried). The permissibility to leave after prayer before burial without permission is discussed as disliked in some views.

Key Terms
الإعادة (al-i'adah): Repeating the janazah prayer, permissible under conditions.
الولي (al-wali): The guardian of the deceased, who has primary right to lead the janazah prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When can the guardian repeat the janazah prayer?
A) If he gave permission to the imam.
B) If he did not give permission and did not follow.
C) Always, even if he followed.
D) Only if the imam was not from the same city.

Key Takeaway
The guardian may repeat the janazah prayer only if he did not give permission and did not participate; others do not repeat.

Guardian’s Precedence Over Deceased’s Recommendation in Janazah
Ruling on preference between guardian and recommended imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi ruling on the validity of a deceased’s recommendation of an imam for janazah and identify the dissenting view from the Nawadir.

Core Idea
The guardian’s right to lead janazah overrides the deceased’s personal wish.

When a person passes away, their family or guardian usually arranges the funeral prayer. Sometimes the deceased may have expressed a wish for a particular person to lead the prayer. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position: such a recommendation is not binding; the guardian’s right of precedence is stronger. A minority narration suggests otherwise, but the relied-upon fatwa follows the majority view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
Who are the two contenders for leading the janazah? The guardian (wali) and the person recommended by the deceased.
2
State the mufta bihi ruling
According to the relied-upon fatwa, the guardian is more entitled (أحق) than the recommended person.
3
Explain the reason
The recommendation is invalid (باطلة) as per the fatwa, so it does not affect the guardian’s right.
4
Note the dissenting view
In the Nawadir of Ibn Rustam, a narration allows the recommendation (الوصية جائزة). This is a weak/less relied-upon view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن له ولاية التقدم فيها أحق ممن أوصى له الميت بالصلاة عليه على المفتى به، لأن الوصية باطلة على المفتى به، قاله الصدر الشهيد، وفي نوادر ابن رستم : الوصية جائزة.
And the one who has the right of precedence in it is more entitled than the one for whom the deceased recommended the prayer over him, according to the fatwa. Because the recommendation is invalid according to the fatwa, as said by al-Sadr al-Shahid. And in the Nawadir of Ibn Rustam, the recommendation is permissible.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This short ruling states that the proper guardian (who has the right) is more entitled to lead the janazah prayer than someone whom the deceased may have recommended in their will. The reason given is that such a recommendation is invalid according to the relied-upon fatwa (mufta bihi). However, there is a dissenting narration (from Ibn Rustam's Nawadir) that allows it. The author sides with the majority view that the guardian's right supersedes any personal wish of the deceased.

Key Terms
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): A recommendation made by the deceased concerning who should lead their janazah prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, it is valid
B) No, it is invalid
C) Valid only if the guardian agrees
D) Valid if the recommended person is a relative

Key Takeaway
The guardian's right to lead janazah overrides any recommendation by the deceased, as the recommendation is invalid in the mufta bihi view.

Prayer at the Grave When Buried Without Janazah
Ruling on praying janazah at the grave when buried without prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing janazah prayer at the grave, identify the conditions under which it is performed, and distinguish between the views on exhumation.

Core Idea
If buried without janazah prayer, pray at the grave; do not disturb the dead unless earth not yet thrown.

This passage from Nur al-Idah addresses a practical scenario: a person is buried without the janazah prayer. What should be done? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling with conditions, and also notes an internal difference of opinion about exhumation. Understanding this will help you apply the correct procedure in cases where funeral rites were missed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The deceased has been buried but the janazah prayer was not performed. Determine if burial is complete (earth thrown over) or not.
2
Apply the primary ruling
If earth has been thrown over the grave, do not exhume; instead, perform the janazah prayer at the grave. This is the ruling from al-Fath.
The body is considered surrendered to Allah and should not be disturbed.
3
Consider the exception
If earth has NOT been thrown over the grave, the body may be taken out and the prayer performed normally. This is also from al-Fath.
4
Note the alternative view
According to al-Khulasah, even if earth has not been thrown, exhumation is not permitted; instead, prayer at the grave is performed. This is an intra-Hanafi difference.
This view is more cautious.
5
Note the condition and later application
Prayer at the grave is valid only as long as the body has not decomposed. Also, if the janazah was already performed before burial, a second prayer at the grave is allowed. The passage ends with a note on multiple funerals: individual prayers are better than combining.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن دفن بلا صلاة صلي على قبره صلي على قبره: قال في الفتح: هذا إذا أهيل عليه التراب؛ لأنه صار مسلما لمالكه تعالى، وخرج عن أيدينا، فلا يتعرض له، بخلاف ما إذا لم يُهل عليه فإنه يخرج ويصلى عليه، لكن في الخلاصة عن الجامع الصغير للحاكم عبد الرحمن: ولو دفن قبل الغسل أو قبل الصلاة لا ينبش فإن دفنوه و لم يهيلوا عليه حتى علموا أنه لم يغسل لكنهم سووا اللبن، لا ينبش أيضاً، أي ويصلى على قبره ثانياً إذا صلى عليه أولاً [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٩١] وإن لم يغسل ما لم يتفسخ، وإذا اجتمعت الجنائز فالإفراد بالصلاة لكل منها أولى،
And if he is buried without prayer, prayer is performed at his grave. 'Prayer is performed at his grave': He said in al-Fath: This is when earth has been thrown over him, because he has become handed over to his Owner, exalted, and has left our hands, so we do not disturb him. Contrary to when earth has not been thrown over him, then he is taken out and prayer is performed over him. But in al-Khulasah from al-Jami' al-Saghir of al-Hakim Abd al-Rahman: If he is buried before washing or before prayer, he is not exhumed. If they buried him and did not throw earth over him until they knew he was not washed, but they arranged the bricks, he is also not exhumed, meaning prayer is performed at his grave a second time if it was prayed over him first. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi p.591] And if he was not washed, as long as he has not decomposed. And when funerals gather, performing the prayer individually for each is more virtuous.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage deals with the situation where a deceased person is buried without the janazah prayer. The ruling is that one may pray at the grave. The commentary from al-Fath explains that this is only when earth has been thrown over the grave (i.e., burial is complete), because then the body is considered surrendered to Allah and should not be disturbed. If earth has not yet been thrown, the body may be taken out and prayed upon normally. However, another view from al-Khulasah says that even if buried without washing or prayer, the body should not be exhumed; instead, pray at the grave. Even if previously prayed upon, a second prayer at the grave may be performed. The condition is that the body has not decomposed. The last part transitions to the next topic about multiple funerals.

Key Terms
تفسخ (tafassukh): Decomposition of the body after which prayer at the grave is no longer performed
أهيل عليه التراب (uhila 'alayhi al-turab): Earth is thrown over the grave, indicating completion of burial
ينبش (yanbush): Exhumation of the body

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under which condition is it permissible to perform the janazah prayer at the grave rather than exhuming?
A) When the body is not washed
B) When earth has been thrown over the grave
C) When the deceased was a child
D) When the guardian requests it

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits and recommends performing janazah prayer at the grave of one who was buried without it, provided the earth has been thrown and the body has not decomposed, and there is no need for exhumation.

Order of Multiple Funeral Prayers and Burial
Ruling on arranging multiple funerals and burial in one grave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred order for arranging multiple funerals in prayer and burial, and apply it to given scenarios.

Core Idea
Men, then boys, then hermaphrodites, then women – arrange by precedence in prayer, reverse in burial.

When multiple funerals coincide, the Hanafi school prescribes a specific arrangement for combined prayer and burial. This lesson explains the preferred order, which reflects the principle of giving precedence to the most virtuous. Understanding this order ensures proper practice in communal funeral rites.

Guided Path
1
Identify the preferred method
The text begins by stating that performing individual funeral prayers for each deceased is more virtuous (اولى). This is the recommended practice.
Individual prayer is superior; combining is permissible but less reward.
2
Understand the placement in combined prayer
If funerals are combined in one prayer, the deceased are laid in a long row with chests towards the qibla. The imam stands facing the row, at the middle? The text says 'chest of each in front of imam', meaning the imam stands at the head/chest level.
The row is arranged such that the imam faces the chests, not the feet.
3
Memorize the order of placement
The order from closest to farthest from the imam is: men, then boys (صبيان), then hermaphrodites (خناثى), then women.
This order prioritizes those with greater religious status and clarity of gender.
4
Apply the reverse order for burial
When burying multiple bodies in one grave, the order is reversed: women closest to the qibla, then hermaphrodites, then boys, then men farthest? Actually, the text says 'على عكس هذا' – opposite of prayer arrangement. Since in prayer the men are closest to the imam (and thus farthest from the qibla? Need to interpret: the row is towards the qibla, so the men are nearest to the imam, but the imam is behind the row? Typically, the imam stands at the head of the row, and the bodies are placed lengthwise towards qibla. The order is relative to the imam. In burial, the qibla side is the head. The reversed order likely means the men are placed farthest from the qibla? Hanafi texts: in burial, women are placed next to the qibla, then children, then men. But we follow the text: reverse of prayer order.
Imam al-Haskafi states in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: the order in burial is opposite to prayer order.
5
Distinguish the ruling's force
The arrangement is not a condition for validity but a recommended practice (sunnah). Neglecting it without reason may be makruh tanzihan.
If combined prayer is performed without adhering to this order, the prayer remains valid but disliked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا اجتمعت الجنائز فالإفراد بالصلاة لكل منها أولى، ويقدم الأفضل فالأفضل، وإن اجتمعن وصلى عليها مرة جعلها صفا طويلا مما يلى القبلة بحيث يكون صدر كل قُدّام الإمام، وراعى الترتيب، فيجعل الرجال مما يلي الإمام، ثم الصبيان بعدهم ثم الخناثى، ثم النساء، ولو دفنوا بقبر واحد وضعوا على عكس هذا، ولا يقتدي بالإمام من وجده بين تكبيرتين،
And when funerals gather, performing the prayer individually for each is more virtuous. And the best is given precedence. If they gather and he prays over them once, he arranges them as a long row toward the qibla such that the chest of each is in front of the imam, and he observes the order: he places the men next to the imam, then the boys after them, then the hermaphrodites, then the women. And if they are buried in one grave, they are placed in the reverse of this. And one who finds the imam between two takbirs does not follow him...
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage provides guidelines for when multiple janazahs are present. It is preferable to pray for each funeral separately. If combined in one prayer, the deceased are lined up in a single long row with their chests facing the qibla (as the body is laid supine? Actually, the deceased are placed such that their heads are toward the qibla? The text says 'chest of each in front of the imam' meaning the imam stands at the head of the row). The order of placement is: first men (closest to imam), then boys, then hermaphrodites (khunatha), then women. If buried in one grave, the order is reversed (men farthest from qibla? The commentary is not explicit but likely women closest to qibla). The next sentence begins the ruling on catching up in the prayer.

Key Terms
الخناثى (al-khunatha): Hermaphrodites (persons of ambiguous gender)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Women
B) Boys
C) Men
D) Khunatha

Key Takeaway
Arrange multiple funerals in prayer with men closest, then boys, then hermaphrodites, then women; reverse for burial.

Latecomer to Janazah Prayer: Rules of Joining Late
Rulings on late entry into janazah prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a latecomer to janazah prayer should join the imam and what to do if arriving after the fourth takbir.

Core Idea
Wait for the imam's next takbir to join; missing the fourth takbir before salam invalidates the prayer.

The janazah prayer has a unique structure of four takbirs. If you arrive late, you cannot simply join in between. This lesson explains precisely when to enter the prayer and how to complete what you missed, based on the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
You arrive after the imam has started. Determine at which point you find the imam: between two takbirs, after the first takbir, or after the fourth takbir.
The passage covers three main scenarios.
2
Apply the rule for joining
If you find the imam between two takbirs, do not follow him immediately. Wait for his next takbir, then enter with that takbir and follow his supplications.
You must start with a takbir that coincides with the imam's.
3
Determine makeup of missed takbirs
After the imam completes the fourth takbir, you must make up the missed takbirs before the funeral is lifted. You do not repeat the supplications you already said with the imam.
The makeup is only for the missing takbirs, not the full prayer.
4
Know when the prayer is missed entirely
If you arrive after the imam has made the fourth takbir but before the salam, the prayer is considered missed. You cannot join, and you must perform the janazah prayer on your own later if possible.
The sound opinion (al-sahih) is that the prayer is invalid in this case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يقتدي بالإمام من وجده بين تكبيرتين، بل ينتظر تكبير الإمام، فيدخل معه، ويوافقه في دعائه، ثم يقضي ما فاته قبل رفع الجنازة، ولا ينتظر تكبير الإمام من حضر تحريمته، ومن حضر بعد التكبيرة الرابعة قبل السلام فاتته الصلاة في الصحيح، وتكره الصلاة عليه في مسجد الجماعة وهو فيه، أو خارجه وبعض الناس في المسجد على المختار
And one who finds the imam between two takbirs does not follow him, but rather waits for the imam's takbir, then enters with him, and agrees with him in his supplication, then makes up what he missed before the funeral is lifted. And one who is present from (the imam's) first takbir does not wait for the imam's takbir. And one who arrives after the fourth takbir before the salam, the prayer has escaped him according to the sound opinion. And it is disliked to pray over him in the congregational mosque while he (the deceased) is inside it, or outside while some people are inside the mosque according to the preferred view.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage rules on when someone arrives late to the janazah prayer. If you find the imam in between two takbirs (i.e., after the first but before the second), you should not start praying immediately. Instead, wait for the imam's next takbir, then enter with him, follow his supplication, and after the imam completes the fourth takbir, you make up the missed takbirs before the funeral is lifted. However, if you were present from the very first takbir, you follow along without waiting. If you arrive after the fourth takbir but before the salam, the prayer is considered missed (the prayer is invalid) according to the sound opinion. The last sentence transitions to the next lesson about the mosque.

Key Terms
تحريمة (tahrimah): The first takbir of the prayer (the opening takbir) which makes the rest of the prayer binding.
تكبير (takbir): The utterance 'Allahu Akbar' which marks a transition in the prayer.
يقضي (yaqdi): To make up (perform what was missed) after the imam has completed the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If you arrive at a janazah prayer after the imam has made the first takbir and is now in the supplication before the second takbir, what should you do according to the Hanafi school?
A) Immediately say your first takbir and join the prayer.
B) Wait for the imam's second takbir, then say your first takbir and join.
C) Do not join; pray separately after the congregation.
D) Say 'Allahu Akbar' and then catch up by making two takbirs after the imam finishes.

Key Takeaway
The latecomer to janazah prayer must wait for the imam's next takbir to start, and must make up missed takbirs before the funeral is lifted.

Janazah Prayer in the Mosque: Dislike and Its Nuances
Ruling on performing janazah prayer inside the mosque

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on janazah prayer in a mosque, distinguish between karahah tahrimiyyah and tanzihiyyah, and apply the custom exception.

Core Idea
Janazah in the mosque is disliked, but the level depends on the cause, and custom can remove the dislike.

The Hanafi school addresses a common practical scenario: should the funeral prayer be performed inside the mosque? The default view is that it is disliked (makruh), but the nature of that dislike and its grounds require careful analysis. This lesson unpacks the two possible causes—fear of soiling versus occupying the mosque for an unintended purpose—and shows how each leads to a different degree of karahah. We also explore an important exception: when a community customarily prays janazah in the mosque, the ruling shifts to permissible, because the builders are presumed to have consented.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing janazah prayer inside a mosque designated for congregational prayers (masjid al-jama'ah). The default ruling is that it is disliked (makruh). Determine whether the text specifies the type of karahah (tahrimiyyah or tanzihiyyah).
The text mentions two narrations: one says tanzihi, the other tahrimi.
2
Analyze the cause of dislike
The passage gives two possible causes: (1) fear of soiling the mosque, and (2) occupying the mosque with something it was not built for. Each cause yields a different level of karahah. Map the cause to the ruling.
Fear of soiling → tahrimiyyah (stronger); occupying → tanzihiyyah (lighter).
3
Examine exceptions and restrictions
The text notes exceptions: if the imam is outside the mosque (some say no dislike), if the funeral is not brought inside (Shams al-A'imma's view), and crucially, if the community customarily prays janazah in the mosque.
Custom (urf) overrides the dislike when the cause is 'occupying'; it does not override if the cause is 'soiling'.
4
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The preferred view (al-mukhtar) is that it is tanzihi (lighter dislike), as preferred by Ibn al-Humam. However, the text shows that the ruling can vary based on circumstances.
The operative ruling for fatwa today: janazah in mosque is makruh tanzihan unless custom permits.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتكره الصلاة عليه في مسجد الجماعة وهو فيه، أو خارجه وبعض الناس في المسجد على المختار وكراهته تنزيهية في رواية، ورجحها المحقق ابن الهمام، وتحريمية في أخرى، والعلة فيه إن كانت خشية التلويث فهي تحريمية، وإن كانت شغل المسجد بما لم يين له فتنزيهية. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٩٦] على المختار: خلافاً لما أورده النسفي من أن الإمام إذا كان خارج المسجد مع بعض القوم لا يكره بالاتفاق، كما علمت من الكراهة على المختار مراقي الفلاح ٥٩٦] وقال شمس الأيمة: إن الكراهة إنما هي في إدخال الجنازة المسجد. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٩٦] قيده الوافي بما إذا لم يكن معتاداً، فإن اعتاد أهل بلدة الصلاة عليه في المسجد لم يكره؛ لأن لباني المسجد علماً بذلك، وهذا على أن العلة أن المسجد لم يبن له، أما على أن خوف التلويث فلا مراقي الفلاح وحاشية الطحطاوي بتغيير)
And it is disliked to pray over him in the congregational mosque while he is inside it, or outside while some people are inside the mosque according to the preferred view. Its dislike is tanzihi (prohibitively disliked) in one narration, preferred by Ibn al-Humam, and tahrimi (close to haram) in another. The cause: if it is fear of soiling, then it is tahrimi; if it is occupying the mosque with something it was not built for, then tanzihi. [Maraqi al-Falah p.596] According to the preferred view: contrary to what al-Nasafi mentioned that if the imam is outside the mosque with some people, it is not disliked by agreement, as you know from the dislike according to the preferred view. [Maraqi al-Falah p.596] And Shams al-A'imma said: the dislike is only for bringing the funeral into the mosque. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi p.596] Al-Wafi restricted it to when it is not customary; if the people of a town are accustomed to prayer over it in the mosque, it is not disliked, because the builders of the mosque were aware of that. This is according to the cause that the mosque was not built for it, but as for the fear of soiling, it is not (overridden by custom). [Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi with modification]
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of performing the janazah prayer inside a mosque that is used for the five daily congregational prayers. The preferred view (al-mukhtar) is that it is disliked (makruh). There is a difference of opinion on the nature of the dislike: some scholars say it is tanzihi (lesser dislike), while others say it is tahrimi (greater dislike, closer to forbidden). The reason for the dislike is either the risk of soiling the mosque or the fact that the mosque was not built for funeral prayers. If the cause is soiling, it is tahrimi; if it's just occupying the mosque, it is tanzihi. However, if the imam himself is outside the mosque with some people, some say it is not disliked at all (as per al-Nasafi). Shams al-A'imma restricts the dislike only to bringing the funeral inside. Importantly, if it is the custom of the town to pray in the mosque, then it is not disliked because the builders knew of this usage. This applies only if the issue is the purpose of the mosque; if the real concern is soiling, custom does not override.

Key Terms
الكراهة التحريمية (al-karahah al-tahrimiyyah): A stronger level of dislike close to haram (prohibited)
الكراهة التنزيهية (al-karahah al-tanzihiyyah): A lighter level of dislike, better to avoid
العلة (al-illah): The cause or reason underlying a ruling
العرف (al-urf): Custom or habitual practice of a community

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a condition for janazah prayer in a mosque to be disliked?
A) The imam is outside the mosque.
B) The community customarily prays janazah in the mosque.
C) The imam is inside the mosque or some people are inside.
D) The funeral bier is not brought into the mosque.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on janazah prayer in a mosque is nuanced: generally disliked, but the level depends on the cause, and community custom can lift the dislike entirely.
