Burial in Houses and Fasaqi Structures
Rulings on burial in houses and fasaqi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on burial in houses and fasaqi structures and identify the reasons for the dislike.

Core Idea
Burial in houses is a privilege of prophets; for others it is disliked.

This lesson addresses two specific burial practices: burying in houses and burying in vaulted structures called fasaqi. The Hanafi school strongly discourages both, citing their exclusivity to prophets and other practical harms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Burial in houses and burial in fasaqi. The ruling for both is makruh (disliked).
The text uses 'يكره' which indicates dislike.
2
Identify the reasoning for houses
Why is burial in houses disliked? Because it is specific to prophets. The text states it is 'خاص بالأنبياء'.
This is a strong reason, making it makruh tahrimi.
3
Note the exception for necessity
Burying more than one in a grave is permissible if necessary, but normally disliked.
4
Analyze the reasons for fasaqi
Four reasons: absence of lahd, multiple burials without necessity, mixing genders, building over graves.
These are specific to fasaqi structures.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكره الدفن في البيوت لاختصاصه بالأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام ويكره الدفن في الفساقي، ولا بأس بدفن أكثر من واحد في قبر للضرورة. ويكره الدفن في البيوت قال الكمال: لا يدفن صغير ولا كبير في البيت الذي مات فيه، فإن ذلك خاص بالأنبياء الالا، بل يدفن في مقابر المسلمين. الفساقي: قال في "فتح القدير": ويكره الدفن في الأماكن التي تسمى فساقي، وهي كبيت معقود بالبناء يسع جماعة قياما ونحوه والكراهة من وجوه: الأول: عدم اللحد، والثاني: دفن الجماعة في قبر واحد لغير ضرورة، الثالث: اختلاط الرجال بالنساء من غير حاجز كما هو الواقع في كثير منها، الرابع: تخصيصها والبناء عليها.
Burial in houses is disliked because it is specific to prophets, peace be upon them. Burial in fasaqi (structures like canopies) is disliked. There is no harm in burying more than one in a grave due to necessity. Burial in houses is disliked; al-Kamal said: No small or big person should be buried in the house where he died, for that is specific to the prophets, but should be buried in Muslim cemeteries. Fasaqi: said in Fath al-Qadir: Burial is disliked in places called fasaqi, which are like a vaulted building accommodating a group standing, etc. The dislike is due to several reasons: first, absence of lahd; second, burying more than one in a grave without necessity; third, mixing of men and women without a barrier as often occurs; fourth, reserving them and building over them.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage prohibits burial in houses, as it is a privilege reserved for prophets. All Muslims, regardless of status, should be buried in public cemeteries. Burial in fasaqi (covered structures) is also disliked because they often lack proper lahd (side niche), they lead to multiple burials in one grave without necessity, they may cause intermixing of genders, and they encourage building over graves. The default is to bury in standard graves in Muslim cemeteries.

Key Terms
فساقي (fasaqi): Vaulted structures built over graves, often used for multiple burials.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is inconvenient
B) It is specific to prophets

D) It is forbidden in Quran

Key Takeaway

Reusing Graves: The Hanafi Dispute After Decomposition
Ruling on multiple burials and reuse after decomposition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reusing a grave after body decomposition and explain the intra-madhhab dispute between al-Zayla'i and al-Tatarkhaniyya.

Core Idea
Reusing a grave after full decomposition is permitted by the preferred Hanafi view due to overwhelming practical necessity.

This passage from Nur al-Idah addresses the sensitive issue of reusing graves and burying multiple bodies in one grave. While initial multiple burial is only allowed for necessity, the question of reusing a grave after the first occupant has turned to dust sparks a debate within the Hanafi school. The author weighs practical necessity against lingering sanctity, ultimately favoring permissibility—especially in crowded urban settings.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling on initial multiple burial
Identify the baseline: burying more than one in a single grave is permitted only for genuine necessity (e.g., disaster, space shortage). Exhumation before decomposition is strictly prohibited as it violates the deceased's honor.
This is the agreed-upon starting point before the dispute arises.
2
Identify the intra-madhhab dispute
After complete decomposition (bala), two positions appear: al-Zayla'i permits reuse; al-Tatarkhaniyya dislikes it (karahah). Note the opposing scholars and their reasoning.
Al-Zayla'i focuses on the removal of the body; al-Tatarkhaniyya insists on remaining sanctity.
3
Analyze each position's evidence
Al-Zayla'i argues that when the body becomes dust, nothing remains to be honored, so reuse, planting, and building are allowed. Al-Tatarkhaniyya holds that even bones retain sanctity, so burial dislike persists.
Both use qiyas: al-Zayla'i analogizes to dust; al-Tatarkhaniyya to intact bones.
4
Understand the author's tarjih
The author (likely Ibn Abidin) favors al-Zayla'i's view, citing 'great difficulty' (mashaqqah ʿazimah) if every grave were permanently reserved. He makes permissibility contingent on bala.
Tarjih mechanism: practical necessity overrides abstract sanctity in the absence of physical remains.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The dispute matters most in large cities where cemetery space is scarce. Under the preferred view, once bodies decompose, graves can be recycled. Under the disliked view, new graves must be dug indefinitely.
This explains why the author explicitly highlights difficulty in 'great cities' (amṣār kabīrah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بأس بدفن أكثر من واحد في قبر للضرورة. ولا بأس بدفن إلخ ما يفعله جهلة الحفارين من نبش القبور التي لم تبل أربابها، وإدخال أجانب عليهم فهو من المنكر الظاهر، وليس من الضرورة المبيحة لجمع ميتين فأكثر ابتداءً في قبر واحد قصد دفن الرجل مع قريبه أو ضيق المحل في تلك المقبرة مع وجود غيرها وإن كانت مما يتبرك بالدفن فيها، فضلا عن كون ذلك ونحوه مبيحا للنبش، وإدخال البعض على البعض قبل البلا مع ما فيه من هتك حرمة الميت الأول وتفريق أجزائه، فالحذر من ذلك، وقال الزيلعي ولو بلي الميت وصار تراباً جاز دفن غيره في قبره وزرعه والبناء عليه. قال في الإمداد : يخالفه ما في "التتارخانية : إذا صار الميت ترابا في القبر يكره دفن غيره في قبره؛ لأن الحرمة باقية، وإن جمعوا عظامه في ناحية، ثم دفن غيره فيه تبركا بالجيران الصالحين ويوجد موضع فارغ يكره ذلك، قلت: لكن في هذا مشقة عظيمة، فالأولى إناطة الجواز بالبلا؛ إذ لا يمكن أن يعد لكل ميت قبر لا يدفن فيه غيره وإن صار الأول ترابا، لا سيما في الأمصار الكبيرة الجامعة، وإلا لزم أن تعم القبور السهل والوعر على أن المنع من الحفر إلى أن لا يبقى عظم وإن أمكن ذلك لبعض الناس، لكن الكلام في جعله حكماً عاماً لكل أحد، فتأمل.
There is no harm in burying more than one in a grave due to necessity. 'There is no harm' etc. The actions of ignorant gravediggers who exhume graves that have not decayed and insert others is an open evil, and it is not the necessity that permits initially gathering two or more in one grave for the purpose of burying a man with his relative or narrowness of the cemetery while other places exist, even if it is blessed to be buried there. This is even more so for exhumation, inserting one after another before decomposition, which violates the honor of the first deceased and dismembers his parts. So beware of that. Al-Zayla'i said: If the deceased has decomposed and become dust, it is permissible to bury another in his grave, plant, and build upon it. In al-Imdad: contrary to what is in al-Tatarkhaniyya: if the deceased becomes dust in the grave, it is disliked to bury another in his grave because the sanctity remains. Even if they gather his bones in a corner and then bury another, if there is space, it is disliked. I say: but in this there is great difficulty, so it is better to make permissibility contingent upon decomposition; because it is impossible to assign each dead a grave that no other will use after the first becomes dust, especially in large cities. Otherwise, graves would spread over the land. The prohibition of digging until no bone remains, even if possible for some, is not a general ruling.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage discusses when multiple burials in one grave are allowed. Initially, burying more than one in a single grave is only permissible due to necessity, such as a disaster or lack of space. It is forbidden to exhume a grave that has not fully decomposed to insert another body. After complete decomposition (the body turns to dust), there is a dispute. Al-Zayla'i permits reuse, while al-Tatarkhaniyya dislikes it due to lingering sanctity. The author (possibly Ibn Abidin) favors permissibility to avoid practical hardship, especially in crowded cities. The solution is to wait until only bones remain and collect them aside before reusing the grave.

Key Terms
بلى (bala): Complete decomposition of the body into dust.
نبش القبر (nabsh al-qabr): Exhumation of a grave.
حرمة (hurma): Sanctity; inviolability of a deceased's grave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in the Hanafi school from this lesson, when is it permissible to bury another person in a grave after the first body has decomposed?
A) Immediately after burial
B) After one year
C) When the body has fully turned to dust (bala)
D) It is never permissible

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits reusing a grave after full decomposition (bala), especially in crowded cities, though a minority view dislikes it due to remaining sanctity.

Writing on Graves and Reciting Quran at Graves
Rulings on graves: writing and Quran recitation with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on writing on graves and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on reciting Quran at graves, identifying the mufta bihi position and its evidence.

Core Idea
Writing on graves is permissible when needed; reciting Quran at graves is not makruh according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

What should we do about writing on graves or reciting Quran there? This passage from Nur al-Idah addresses both. While a hadith prohibits writing, the Hanafi school allows it if necessary to preserve the trace. For recitation, there is a famous difference between Abu Hanifa and his student Muhammad. You will see how later scholars resolved it and how innovation changes the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
The passage discusses two separate matters: writing on graves and reciting Quran at graves. Identify each and note the initial ruling stated.
2
Understand the basis for writing
Note the hadith prohibition (dalil naqli) and the differentiation in Al-Muhit: need vs. no excuse. Identify the conditions that make it permissible.
This shows how a general prohibition can be qualified by necessity.
3
Map the intra-Hanafi dispute on recitation
Identify the positions: Abu Hanifa (makruh), Muhammad (not makruh). Determine which view was adopted by later mashayikh and why.
The tarjih is based on practice of pious predecessors and the principle of ease.
4
Distinguish bare recitation from recitation with innovations
The passage adds that when recitation is accompanied by innovations, it becomes makruh. Understand why the context matters.
This is a critical qualification often missed.
5
Apply the rulings
Given a scenario, determine whether writing or recitation is permissible, makruh, or prohibited based on the conditions.
Practice leads to mastery.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بأس بالكتابة عليه لئلا يذهب الأثر ولا يمتهن ويكره الدفن في البيوت لاختصاصه بالأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام ويكره الدفن في الفساقي، ولا بأس بدفن أكثر من واحد في قبر للضرورة "الولوالجي"، ولعلك الاستيجار ولا بأس إلخ: قال في "البحر": الحديث المتقدم يمنع الكتابة، فليكن هو المعول عليه، لكن فصل في "المحيط": فقال: إن احتيج إلى الكتابة حتى لا يذهب الأثر ولا يمتهن به جازت، فأما الكتابة من غير عذر فلا [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦١١] بالكتابة عليه: وهل قراءة القرآن عند القبور مكروهة، تكلموا فيه: قال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله يكره، وقال محمد: لا يكره، ومشايخنا أخذوا بقول محمد رحمه الله رجل مات فأجلس وارثه رجلا يقرأ القرآن على قبره تكلموا فيه: منهم من كره ذلك، والمختار أنه ليس بمكروه، ويكون المأخوذ في هذا الباب قول محمد رحمه الله، ولهذا حكي عن الشيخ أبي بكر العياض أنه أوصى عند موته بذلك، ولو كان مكروهاً لما أوصى به، هذا ما في "الشبلي" نقلا عن عرفت أن هذا الاختلاف في مجرد القراءة، فقال الإمام هو مكروه، وأما ما شاع في بلادنا الهندية لقراءة القرآن مع محدثات أخر فمكروه قطعا خلافا لمن جعل البدعات رزقه.
There is no harm in writing on it (the grave) so that the trace does not disappear and it is not dishonored. Burial in houses is disliked due to its being specific to the Prophets, peace and blessings be upon them. Burial in waterways/irrigation canals is disliked. There is no harm in burying more than one in a grave out of necessity. Al-Walwaliji said... and perhaps... He said in Al-Bahr: The aforementioned hadith prohibits writing, so it should be relied upon, but he differentiated in Al-Muhit: If there is need for writing so that the trace does not disappear and it is not dishonored, it is permissible. As for writing without an excuse, it is not [permissible]. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 611] On writing on it: Is reciting Quran at graves disliked? They discussed it: Abu Hanifa said it is disliked, Muhammad said it is not disliked, and our scholars adopted the view of Muhammad. A man died and his heir hired a man to recite Quran at his grave; they discussed it: some disliked it, but the chosen opinion is that it is not disliked. The adopted view in this matter is the view of Muhammad. For this reason it is narrated that Sheikh Abu Bakr al-Ayyad willed that at his death, and if it were disliked, he would not have willed it. This is what is in Al-Shubli transmitted from... You know that this difference is about mere recitation; the Imam said it is disliked. As for what is common in our Indian lands of reciting Quran with other innovations, it is definitely disliked, contrary to those who make innovations their livelihood.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage presents rulings on two related issues: writing on graves and reciting Quran at graves. The author first states that writing on graves is permissible if needed to preserve the trace and prevent dishonor, quoting Al-Walwaliji. The commentary from Al-Bahr notes that a hadith prohibits writing, so that must be relied upon, but Al-Muhit distinguishes: if there is a need, it is permissible; without excuse, it is not. Regarding reciting Quran at graves, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa considers it makruh, while Muhammad (al-Shaybani) does not. The later scholars (mashayikh) adopted Muhammad's view, making it the mufta bihi. The commentator supports this by citing a pious predecessor who willed it. However, the commentator warns that when recitation is accompanied by innovations, it is definitely makruh.

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): An action that is disliked and discouraged; avoiding it is rewarded but doing it is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Yes, it is makruh tanzihi
B) No, it is not makruh
C) It is haram
D) It is wajib

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi view permits writing on graves when needed and considers Quran recitation at graves not makruh, but warns against accompanying innovations.

Burial in Houses: Ruling and Evidence
Ruling with proof: burial in houses is disliked

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on burial in houses and explain the evidence for its disliked status.

Core Idea
Burial in houses is reserved for Prophets; the Ummah must be buried in public cemeteries.

The Hanafi school considers burial in houses to be makruh tanzihi (disliked) because it emulates a practice exclusive to Prophets. In this lesson, we examine the ruling and its basis from the text of Nur al-Idah and its commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is burying a deceased person in a house. The ruling is makruh (disliked).
Makruh tanzihi: not sinful but contrary to the preferred practice.
2
Locate the evidence
The evidence given is that burial in houses is 'specific to the Prophets' (خاص بالأنبياء). This indicates that it is not for the general Muslim community.
This is derived from the sunna that Prophets are buried where they die.
3
Understand the scope
The ruling applies to all non-prophets, regardless of age or status. Al-Kamal explicitly says no small or big should be buried in the house.
4
Note exceptions
No exception is mentioned for houses; the only exception for group burial in one grave is for necessity (mentioned later in the text but not for houses).
If there is no cemetery available, necessity may apply but the text does not address that.
5
Apply to contemporary practice
Today, burial at home (e.g., in a backyard) would be considered makruh. The proper practice is to bury in the public Muslim cemetery.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكره الدفن في البيوت لاختصاصه بالأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام ويكره الدفن في الفساقي، ولا بأس بدفن أكثر من واحد في قبر للضرورة "الولوالجي"، ولعلك الاستيجار ولا بأس إلخ: قال في "البحر": الحديث المتقدم يمنع الكتابة، فليكن هو المعول عليه، لكن فصل في "المحيط": فقال: إن احتيج إلى الكتابة حتى لا يذهب الأثر ولا يمتهن به جازت، فأما الكتابة من غير عذر فلا [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦١١] بالكتابة عليه: وهل قراءة القرآن عند القبور مكروهة، تكلموا فيه: قال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله يكره، وقال محمد: لا يكره، ومشايخنا أخذوا بقول محمد رحمه الله رجل مات فأجلس وارثه رجلا يقرأ القرآن على قبره تكلموا فيه: منهم من كره ذلك، والمختار أنه ليس بمكروه، ويكون المأخوذ في هذا الباب قول محمد رحمه الله، ولهذا حكي عن الشيخ أبي بكر العياض أنه أوصى عند موته بذلك، ولو كان مكروهاً لما أوصى به، هذا ما في "الشبلي" نقلا عن عرفت أن هذا الاختلاف في مجرد القراءة، فقال الإمام هو مكروه، وأما ما شاع في بلادنا الهندية لقراءة القرآن مع محدثات أخر فمكروه قطعا خلافا لمن جعل البدعات رزقه. ويكره الدفن في البيوت قال الكمال: لا يدفن صغير ولا كبير في البيت الذي مات فيه، فإن ذلك خاص بالأنبياء عليهم السلام، بل يدفن في مقابر المسلمين. مراقي الفلاح: ٦١٢] الفساقي: قال في "فتح القدير": ويكره الدفن في الأماكن التي تسمى فساقي، وهي كبيت معقود بالبناء يسع جماعة قياما ونحوه والكراهة من وجوه: الأول: عدم اللحد، والثاني: دفن الجماعة في قبر واحد لغير ضرورة، الثالث: اختلاط الرجال بالنساء من غير حاجز كما هو الواقع في كثير منها، الرابع: تخصيصها والبناء عليها. [البحر الرائق: ٣٠٧/٢]
Burial in houses is disliked, because it is specific to the Prophets. Burial in fasaqi is disliked. There is no harm in burying more than one in a grave out of necessity. Al-Walwaliji said... and perhaps... He said in Al-Bahr: The aforementioned hadith prohibits writing, so it should be relied upon, but he differentiated in Al-Muhit... [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 611] On writing on it... [repeated text] Burial in houses is disliked. Al-Kamal said: Neither small nor big should be buried in the house he died in, for that is particular to the Prophets, rather they should be buried in Muslim cemeteries. [Maraqi al-Falah: 612] Fasaqi: He said in Fath al-Qadir: Burial in places called fasaqi is disliked. They are like a building roofed, accommodating a group standing, etc. The dislike is from several aspects: first, lack of proper tomb/lahd; second, burying a group in one grave without necessity; third, intermingling of men and women without a barrier as is common in many of them; fourth, singling them out and building upon them. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/307]
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage provides two rulings on where burial is disliked. First, burial in houses is generally disliked, as it is a practice exclusive to prophets. Al-Kamal stresses that no one, child or adult, should be buried in the house where they died; they must be buried in the public cemetery. Second, burial in structures called 'fasaqi' (plural of fisqiyya, meaning water conduits or catacombs) is disliked for four reasons: they often lack a proper lahd (side niche), they lead to burying multiple bodies in one grave without necessity, men and women mix without a partition, and they are often singled out and built upon, which is prohibited. The passage thus guides Muslims to avoid such burial places and adhere to standard cemetery burials.

Key Terms
خاص بالأنبياء (khaas bil-anbiyaa): Specific to the Prophets; a privilege or characteristic that applies only to Prophets.
مقابر المسلمين (maqabir al-muslimin): Muslim cemeteries, the designated place for burying the deceased according to sunna.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is burial in houses makruh according to Al-Kamal?
A) It is too expensive
B) It is specific to Prophets
C) It is unsanitary
D) It causes overcrowding in cities

Key Takeaway
Burial in houses is disliked because it imitates a practice exclusive to Prophets; Muslims should be buried in public cemeteries.

Burial in Fasaqi: Four Reasons for Dislike
Ruling with proof: burial in fasaqi is disliked for four reasons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four reasons for disliking burial in fasaqi and apply the ruling to contemporary burial structures.

Core Idea
Fasaqi are disliked because they lack proper graves, mix genders, and encourage building on graves.

The term 'fasaqi' refers to vaulted burial structures that accommodate multiple bodies. The Hanafi school explains that burial in such places is makruh tanzihi for four specific reasons, each based on sunna or general principles. This lesson breaks down those reasons.

Guided Path
1
Define fasaqi
Fasaqi are structures like vaulted buildings that can hold several standing people; they are used for burial.
The word is plural of fisqiya, originally meaning water conduit, but here refers to catacomb-like structures.
2
Identify the overall ruling
Burial in fasaqi is declared makruh (disliked).
Makruh tanzihi: not sinful but contrary to the preferred practice.
3
Analyze each of the four reasons
The text from Fath al-Qadir lists four specific reasons: 1) lack of proper lahd (side niche), 2) burying multiple people in one grave without necessity, 3) intermingling of men and women without a barrier, 4) singling them out and building upon them.
4
Understand the underlying principles
Proper burial sunna includes: individual graves with lahd, segregation of genders, and prohibition of permanent structures over graves. Each reason violates one of these.
These are derived from hadith and established practice.
5
Apply to modern equivalents
Today, family mausoleums or public vaults that compromise these principles are considered makruh. Simple graves in open cemeteries are preferred.

اللحد (al-lahd): A side niche dug into the grave wall to place the body, which is the sunna method of burial.

Burying Multiple Persons and Exhuming Graves: Necessity and Decay
Rulings on multiple burials and exhumation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on burying multiple persons in one grave and identify the condition that permits exhumation.

Core Idea
Burying more than one in a grave is only allowed for necessity; exhumation before decay is forbidden.

This lesson examines the rulings on multiple burials and exhumation. The Hanafi school strictly limits these practices to necessity and decay. We will explore the key conditions and the scholarly disagreements within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: burying multiple persons in one grave and exhuming old graves. The default ruling is that each body should have its own grave and graves should not be disturbed.
This is the baseline before exceptions.
2
Recognize the exception of necessity
The text states it is permissible to bury more than one in a grave out of necessity (darurah). Understand what constitutes necessity: e.g., lack of space, emergency.
Necessity overrides the default prohibition.
3
Analyze the condition of decay (bala)
For exhumation and reusing a grave, the body must have completely decayed to dust. Al-Zayla'i allows this; Al-Tatarkhaniya dislikes it. The commentator (Radd al-Muhtar) prefers permissibility tied to decay due to public need.
Decay is the key condition for permissibility.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a difference of opinion on whether the sanctity of the grave remains after decay. The relied-upon position is that after decay, it becomes permissible to bury another.
The later fatwa favors decay as the criterion.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Based on the commentator's tarjih, the operative ruling is that multiple burial for necessity is allowed during life, and after death, exhumation and reburial are permissible once decay is confirmed.
This balances practical needs with respect for the deceased.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بأس بدفن أكثر من واحد في قبر للضرورة "الولوالجي"، ولعلك الاستيجار ولا بأس إلخ: قال في "البحر": الحديث المتقدم يمنع الكتابة، فليكن هو المعول عليه، لكن فصل في "المحيط": فقال: إن احتيج إلى الكتابة حتى لا يذهب الأثر ولا يمتهن به جازت، فأما الكتابة من غير عذر فلا [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦١١] بالكتابة عليه: وهل قراءة القرآن عند القبور مكروهة، تكلموا فيه: قال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله يكره، وقال محمد: لا يكره، ومشايخنا أخذوا بقول محمد رحمه الله رجل مات فأجلس وارثه رجلا يقرأ القرآن على قبره تكلموا فيه: منهم من كره ذلك، والمختار أنه ليس بمكروه، ويكون المأخوذ في هذا الباب قول محمد رحمه الله، ولهذا حكي عن الشيخ أبي بكر العياض أنه أوصى عند موته بذلك، ولو كان مكروهاً لما أوصى به، هذا ما في "الشبلي" نقلا عن عرفت أن هذا الاختلاف في مجرد القراءة، فقال الإمام هو مكروه، وأما ما شاع في بلادنا الهندية لقراءة القرآن مع محدثات أخر فمكروه قطعا خلافا لمن جعل البدعات رزقه. ويكره الدفن في البيوت قال الكمال: لا يدفن صغير ولا كبير في البيت الذي مات فيه، فإن ذلك خاص بالأنبياء عليهم السلام، بل يدفن في مقابر المسلمين. مراقي الفلاح: ٦١٢] الفساقي: قال في "فتح القدير": ويكره الدفن في الأماكن التي تسمى فساقي، وهي كبيت معقود بالبناء يسع جماعة قياما ونحوه والكراهة من وجوه: الأول: عدم اللحد، والثاني: دفن الجماعة في قبر واحد لغير ضرورة، الثالث: اختلاط الرجال بالنساء من غير حاجز كما هو الواقع في كثير منها، الرابع: تخصيصها والبناء عليها. [البحر الرائق: ٣٠٧/٢] من ولا بأس بدفن إلخ ما يفعله جهلة الحفارين من نبش القبور التي لم تبل أربابها، وإدخال أجانب عليهم فهو من المنكر الظاهر، وليس من الضرورة المبيحة لجمع ميتين فأكثر ابتداءً في قبر واحد قصد دفن الرجل مع قريبه أو ضيق المحل في تلك المقبرة مع وجود غيرها وإن كانت مما يتبرك بالدفن فيها، فضلا عن كون ذلك ونحوه مبيحا للنبش، وإدخال البعض على البعض قبل البلا مع ما فيه من هتك حرمة الميت الأول وتفريق أجزائه، فالحذر من ذلك، وقال الزيلعي ولو بلي الميت وصار تراباً جاز دفن غيره في قبره وزرعه والبناء عليه. قال في الإمداد : يخالفه ما في "التتارخانية : إذا صار الميت ترابا في القبر يكره دفن غيره في قبره؛ لأن الحرمة باقية، وإن جمعوا عظامه في ناحية، ثم دفن غيره فيه تبركا بالجيران الصالحين ويوجد موضع فارغ يكره ذلك، قلت: لكن في هذا مشقة عظيمة، فالأولى إناطة الجواز بالبلا؛ إذ لا يمكن أن يعد لكل ميت قبر لا يدفن فيه غيره وإن صار الأول ترابا، لا سيما في الأمصار الكبيرة الجامعة، وإلا لزم أن تعم القبور السهل والوعر على أن المنع من الحفر إلى أن لا يبقى عظم وإن أمكن ذلك لبعض الناس، لكن الكلام في جعله حكماً عاماً لكل أحد، فتأمل. [رد المحتار: ٣٣٣/٢] عسر جداً،
There is no harm in burying more than one in a grave out of necessity. Al-Walwaliji said... and perhaps... [repeated text from earlier] From: 'There is no harm in burying' etc. What ignorant gravediggers do of exhuming graves whose occupants have not decayed and inserting strangers is manifest evil. It is not a necessity permitting the initial gathering of two or more in one grave for the purpose of burying a man with his relative or the narrowness of the place in that cemetery while other cemeteries exist, even if it is considered blessed to be buried there, much less that such would permit exhumation and inserting others before decay, along with the violation of the sanctity of the first deceased and the scattering of his parts. So beware of that. Al-Zayla'i said: If the deceased has decayed and become dust, it is permissible to bury another in his grave, to plant, and to build upon it. He said in Al-Imdad: Contrary to what is in Al-Tatarkhaniya: If the deceased becomes dust in the grave, it is disliked to bury another in his grave because the sanctity remains. And if they gather his bones in a corner, then bury another in it seeking blessing from righteous neighbors, and there is an empty spot, it is disliked. I say: But in this is great difficulty, so the better approach is to tie permissibility to decay, as it is impossible to assign a grave to each deceased that will not be used for another even if the first becomes dust, especially in large crowded cities. Otherwise, graves would cover plains and rough lands, and the prohibition from digging until no bone remains, although possible for some people, is not a general ruling for everyone. Ponder. [Radd al-Muhtar: 2/333] Very difficult.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage addresses when multiple bodies can be buried in one grave and the prohibition of exhuming graves. The author reiterates that burying more than one in a grave is only allowed out of dire necessity. The commentary strongly condemns the practice of ignorant gravediggers who dig up graves before the body has decayed and insert others, calling it manifest evil (munkar). It is not considered a necessity even if one wants to be buried near a relative or if the cemetery is crowded but other cemeteries exist. However, Al-Zayla'i is quoted as saying that once the body has completely decayed into dust, it is permissible to bury another in the same grave, and even to plant or build over it. But there is a contrary view from Al-Tatarkhaniya that considers it disliked due to the remaining sanctity. The commentator (from Radd al-Muhtar) suggests that due to extreme difficulty in crowded cities, the permissibility should be tied to decay, as a general prohibition would be impractical.

Key Terms
نبش (nabsh): Exhuming a grave, usually forbidden before decay.
بلا (bala): Decay or decomposition of the body in the grave.
ضرورة (darurah): Necessity that permits an otherwise prohibited action.
كراهة تحريمية (karahah tahrimiyyah): Prohibitively disliked; close to haram but with less certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for burying another person in an existing grave according to the preferred view?
A) The first body must be completely decayed
B) The grave must be blessed
C) The second person must be a relative
D) It is always forbidden

Key Takeaway
Multiple burial and exhumation in Hanafi fiqh are governed by necessity and decay; exhumation before decay is forbidden, but after decay it becomes permissible due to public need.

Burial at Sea and Transporting the Deceased: Hanafi Rulings
Ruling on sea burial and transport limits with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on burial at sea and transport of the deceased, and identify the exceptional cases where exhumation is permitted.

Core Idea
Transport after burial is forbidden by consensus unless the land is usurped or taken by pre-emption.

This passage from Nur al-Idah and its commentary addresses the practical scenarios of death at sea and the transportation of the deceased. It establishes important distinctions: burial at sea is only allowed when harm is feared, and transporting the body before burial is restricted to a short distance. The most emphatic ruling is the consensus (ijma') that exhumation after burial is absolutely prohibited, with only two specific exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core rulings
The passage covers three main situations: burial at sea, transport before burial, and transport after burial. Identify each and the ruling attached.
2
Determine the hukm for each
Sea burial is mubah when necessary; transport before burial is mubah up to two miles and makruh beyond; transport after burial is haram except for explicit exceptions.
3
Locate the proofs
The main proof for prohibition after burial is ijma' (consensus). For sea burial, the proof is necessity (darura). For transport limits, there are narrations from Aisha and earlier prophets.
4
Note the exceptions
The two agreed exceptions are usurped land/shroud and property taken by shuf'a. A third case (water damage) is disputed, but the mufta bihi is prohibition.
5
Evaluate the authority
The ruling on post-burial transport is supported by ijma', making it binding. The exceptions are based on necessity (haqq al-adami). The transport before burial ruling is based on practice of prophets and companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويحجز بين كل اثنين بالتراب ومن مات في سفينة وكان البر بعيدا وخيف الضرر، غسل وكفن وصلي عليه وألقي في البحر، ويستحب الدفن في مقبرة محل مات به أو قتل، فإن نقل قبل الدفن قدر ميل أو ميلين لا بأس به وكره نقله لأكثر منه، ولا يجوز نقله بعد دفنه بالإجماع، إلا أن تكون الأرض مغصوبة أو أخذت بالشفعة، وإن دفن في قبر حفر لغيره ضمن قيمة الحفر، من الأحياء ويحجز بين كل إلخ أي يجعل بين كل اثنين حاجزا أي حائلا مراقي الفلاح (٦۱۲] وخيف الضرر: أما إذا لم يخف عليه التغير ولو بعد البر أو كان البر قريبا أمكن خروجه فلا والظاهر عليه كما يفيده مفهومه یرمی حرمة رميه حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦١١] ويستحب الدفن إلخ أي المستحب أن يدفن كل في مقبرة البلدة التي مات بها، ونقل عن عائشة رضي الله عنها أنها قالت حين زارت قبر أخيها عبد الرحمن وكان مات بالشام، وحمل منها لو كان الأمر فيك إلى ما نقلتك، ولدفنتك حيث مت، ثم قال المصنف في "التجنيس" في النقل من بلد إلى بلد: لا إثم؛ لما نقل أن يعقوب مات بمصر، فنقل إلى الشام، وموسى عليه السلام نقل تابوت يوسف عليه السلام بعد ما أتى عليه زمان من مصر إلى الشام. [فتح القدير: ١٠١/٢] ولا يجوز إلخ في "المضمرات": النقل بعد الدفن على ثلاثة أوجه في وجه يجوز باتفاق، وفي وجه: لا يجوز باتفاق، وفي وجه: اختلاف أما الأول فهو إذا دفن في أرض مغصوبة، أو كفن في ثوب مغصوب، ولم يرض صاحبه إلا بنقله عن ملكه، أو نزع ثوبه جاز أن يخرج منه باتفاق، وأما الثاني : فكالأم إذا أرادت أن تنظر إلى وجه ولدها، أو نقله إلى مقبرة أخرى، لا يجوز باتفاق، وأما الثالث: إذا غلب الماء على القبر، فقيل: يجوز تحويله؛ لما روي أن صالح بن عبد الله رؤي في المنام، وهو يقول: حوّلوني عن قبري، فقد آذاني الماء ثلاثاً، فنظروا، فإذا شقه الذي يلي الماء قد أصابه الماء، فأفتى ابن عباس رضي الله عنه بتحويله، وقال الفقيه أبو جعفر : يجوز ذلك، ثم رجع ومنع. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦١٥] إلا أن تكون إلخ فيخرج لحق صاحبها؛ لأنه يملك ظاهرها وباطنها، وإن شاء سواه بالأرض، وانتفع بها زراعة أو غيرها مراقي الفلاح: ٦١٥] أو أخذت بالشفعة صورة الشفعة: أن يشتري المتوفي قبل موته أرضا من بائع له شريك فيها أو جار، ثم دفن فيها بعد موته فعلم من له الشفعة فطلبها، فأخذها بالشفعة، وكذا لو اشتراها الوارث أو نحوه [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٦١٥] ضمن قيمة الحفر أي من تركته، وإلا فمن بيت المال أو المسلمين كما قدمناه، فإن كانت المقبرة واسعة يكره ذلك؛ لأن صاحب القبر يستوحش بذلك، وإن كانت الأرض ضيقة جاز، أي بلا كراهة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٦١٥]
And a barrier of earth is placed between every two [bodies]. Whoever dies on a ship and the land is far and harm is feared, he is washed, shrouded, prayed over, and thrown into the sea. It is recommended to bury in the cemetery of the place where he died or was killed. If he is transported before burial the distance of a mile or two, there is no harm, and transporting him more than that is disliked. It is not permissible to transport him after burial by consensus, unless the land was usurped or taken by pre-emption. If he is buried in a grave dug for another, he owes the value of the digging. From the living: 'And a barrier between every two' means a barrier is placed between every two. [Maraqi al-Falah: 612] 'And harm is feared': If no change is feared even after being on land or the land is near and he can be taken out, then it is not [permissible to throw at sea] and the apparent ruling is as indicated by its implication... [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 611] 'It is recommended to bury' etc. It is recommended that each be buried in the cemetery of the town where he died. It is narrated from Aisha that she said when visiting her brother Abd al-Rahman's grave (who died in Sham and was carried to her): 'If I had the choice in your matter, I would not have transported you, and I would have buried you where you died.' Then the author said in Al-Tajnis regarding transportation from one town to another: There is no sin, because it is narrated that Ya'qub died in Egypt and was transported to Sham, and Musa transported the coffin of Yusuf after some time from Egypt to Sham. [Fath al-Qadir: 2/101] 'It is not permissible' etc. In Al-Mudmarat: Transport after burial is of three types: one is permissible by agreement, one is impermissible by agreement, and one is disputed. The first: if buried in usurped land, or shrouded in usurped cloth, and the owner does not agree except by removing it from his property, or removing the cloth, then it is permitted to take him out by agreement. The second: like a mother wanting to see her son's face, or moving him to another cemetery, it is not permissible by agreement. The third: if water overcomes the grave, it is said it is permissible to move him, because it is narrated that Salih ibn Abdullah was seen in a dream saying, 'Move me from my grave, water has harmed me three times,' and they looked and found the side facing water had been affected, so Ibn Abbas gave a fatwa to move him. Abu Ja'far said it is permissible, then retracted and forbade. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 615] 'Unless' etc. It is removed for the right of the owner, because he owns its apparent and interior, and if he wishes he can level it with the ground and benefit from it for cultivation or otherwise. [Maraqi al-Falah: 615] 'Or taken by pre-emption': The form of pre-emption: that the deceased before his death bought land from a seller who has a partner or neighbor in it, then he was buried in it after his death, and the one entitled to pre-emption learns of it and demands it, so he takes it by pre-emption. Likewise if the heir or someone else bought it. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 615] 'He owes the value of the digging': i.e., from his estate; otherwise it is from the public treasury or the Muslims as we have mentioned. If the cemetery is spacious, this is disliked because the owner of the grave would be distressed; if the land is narrow, it is permissible without dislike. [Maraqi al-Falah: 615]
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage covers several burial rulings. First, it recommends placing a barrier of earth between every two bodies in a grave. Second, for a death at sea: if land is far and decay is feared, the body may be washed, shrouded, prayed over, and thrown into the sea. If land is near or no risk, this is not allowed. Third, it is recommended (mustahabb) to bury the dead in the cemetery of the town where they died or were killed. Transporting the body before burial up to a mile or two is permissible; beyond that is makruh. This is supported by narrations of prophets being transported. Fourth, transporting after burial is absolutely forbidden by consensus (ijma'), except in two cases: (1) if the land was usurped, or the shroud was usurped, and the owner demands removal; (2) if the land was taken by pre-emption (shuf'a). There is a third disputed case where water damages the grave. Fifth, if a person is buried in a grave dug for another, the value of the digging must be compensated from his estate. If the cemetery is spacious, such burial is disliked because it distresses the original grave owner; if narrow, it is permissible without dislike.

Key Terms
الشفعة (al-shuf'a): Right of pre-emption: a partner or neighbor can take ownership of sold property by paying the price.
إجماع (ijma'): Consensus of scholars; here, consensus that transport after burial is impermissible except for exceptions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on transporting a deceased person after burial by consensus?
A) Permissible if the family requests
B) Not permissible except in cases of usurped land or pre-emption
C) Permissible up to two miles
D) Always permissible

Key Takeaway
Transport after burial is prohibited by consensus; only two exceptions exist: usurped land or pre-emption.
